Ruling on Sadl (Letting Garment Hang) in Prayer
Ruling on sadl with proof and intra-school variation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sadl, identify the conditions that change its karahah, and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Sadl is makruh tanzih when done arrogantly or negligently, but permitted with a valid excuse.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on sadl—letting one's garment hang loosely during prayer. The text defines the act, explains when it becomes disliked, and presents a dissenting view within the school. A hadith from Abu Hurairah serves as the primary evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sadl: placing the garment on head and shoulders without securing its sides. The ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked), but only when done out of arrogance or negligence.
The ruling changes with an excuse (ʿudhr): then it is not disliked.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith narrated by Abu Hurairah: 'The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) forbade sadl and that a man cover his mouth.' Reported by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim, who authenticated it.
This is a dalil naqli (textual proof) from the Sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition (naha) in the hadith indicates karahah (dislike) in Hanafi usul, as a prohibition from the Prophet (ﷺ) that is not definitive (zanni al-thubut) yields karahah tanzihiyyah.
Hadith is ahad, so it does not reach the level of haram.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Khulasa states that the chosen view (mukhtar) is that sadl is not disliked at all. This shows legitimate difference within the school.
The mufta bihi (operative position) remains that it is makruh without an excuse.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text gives weight to the view that sadl is disliked, but acknowledges the alternative. The later Hanafi masters (fatawa mutakhkhirin) rely on the hadith and consider it makruh tanzih.
The practical fatwa: makruh when done out of carelessness or pride, but permissible with a valid reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُكْرَهُ سَدْلُهُ، يُقَالُ: سَدَلَ الثَّوْبَ سَدْلاً مِنْ بَابِ طَلَبَ، وَأَسْدَلَ خَطَأً. أَيْ: سَدَلَ ثَوْبَهُ تَكَبُّراً أَوْ تَهَاوُناً، وَبِالْعُذْرِ لَا يُكْرَهُ السَّدْلُ. وَهُوَ أَنْ يَجْعَلَ الثَّوْبَ عَلَى رَأْسِهِ وَكَتِفَيْهِ وَيُرْسِلَ جَوَانِبَهُ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يَضُمَّهُمَا. وَفِي شَرْحِ الْوِقَايَةِ: هَذَا فِي الطَّيْلَسَانِ، أَمَّا فِي الْقَبَاءِ وَنَحْوِهِ فَهُوَ أَنْ يُلْقِيَهُ عَلَى كَتِفَيْهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يُدْخِلَ يَدَيْهِ فِي كُمَّيْهِ. وَفِي الْخُلَاصَةِ: الْمُخْتَارُ عَدَمُ كَرَاهَتِهِ. وَذَلِكَ لِقَوْلِ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنِ السَّدْلِ، وَأَنْ يُغَطِّيَ الرَّجُلُ فَاهُ» رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ وَالْحَاكِمُ وَصَحَّحَهُ.
And letting it hang (sadl) is disliked. It is said: sadl of the garment is from bab talaba, and 'asdala' is a mistake. That is, letting his garment hang out of arrogance or negligence, and with an excuse it is not disliked. It is to place the garment on his head and shoulders and let its sides hang without gathering them. In Sharh al-Wiqaya: this applies to the taylasan; as for the qaba' and the like, it is to throw it over his shoulders without inserting his hands into its sleeves. In al-Khulasa: the chosen view is that it is not disliked. This is due to Abu Hurairah's statement: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade sadl and that a man cover his mouth.' Reported by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim, and he declared it authentic.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage covers sadl, which is letting the garment hang loosely. The ruling is that it is disliked (makruh) when done out of arrogance or negligence, but not disliked when there is an excuse. The prohibition is from a hadith of Abu Hurairah. However, there is also a view from al-Khulasa that it is not disliked at all. The text explains the physical form of sadl: placing the garment on head and shoulders without securing it. Some scholars distinguish between types of garments. The overall ruling is that it is makruh unless there is a valid reason.

Key Terms
السَّدْل (al-sadl): Letting the garment hang loosely over shoulders without securing it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is sadl (letting garment hang) not disliked in prayer?
A) When done out of arrogance.
B) When there is a valid excuse.
C) It is always disliked.
D) When performed with a turban.

Key Takeaway
Sadl is makruh tanzih only when done out of pride or carelessness, but permissible with a valid excuse; the hadith provides the evidence, but an intra-Hanafi difference exists.

The Disliked Act of Sadl in Prayer
Defining Sadl, its prohibition in prayer, and the conditions of karahah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Sadl, state its ruling in Hanafi fiqh, identify the conditions that affect its karahah, and apply the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Letting your garment hang loose in prayer is disliked if done carelessly, but excused if needed.

This lesson examines the ruling of Sadl – the practice of wearing an outer garment loosely slumped over the shoulders without securing it, a common habit during prayer. The Hanafi school deems it makruh tanzihi in certain conditions, but not when there is a legitimate need. Understanding when the ruling applies helps avoid unnecessary sin while accommodating valid excuses. The proof is a hadith prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Sadl is defined as placing the garment on the head and shoulders and letting the sides hang without folding. The ruling is makruh (disliked).
The text uses 'يكره' indicating dislike.
2
Distinguish intentional vs. excused
The dislike applies when done out of arrogance or carelessness (تكبراً أو تهاوناً). With an excuse (عذر), it is not disliked.
This nuance shows the ruling is not absolute.
3
Understand varying definitions
Different garments (taylasan, qaba') have slight differences in definition. For a taylasan, it is worn like a hood; for a coat, it is thrown over shoulders without inserting arms.
The text cites Sharh al-Wiqaya for these distinctions.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some later Hanafi scholars (al-Khulasa) hold that Sadl is not disliked at all. The more correct view (al-ashah) is that it is disliked, as per Majma' al-Riwayat and al-Bahr.
The author sides with the majority.
5
Connect to the hadith proof
The prohibition is from Abu Huraira: the Prophet (ﷺ) prohibited Sadl and covering the mouth. This hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim.
The hadith is ahad, so the ruling is makruh tanzihi, not haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يكره (سَدْلُهُ)، يقال: سدل الثوب سدلاً، من باب طلب، وأسدل خطأ كذا في الدراية»، أي: سدل ثوبه تكبراً أو تهاوناً، وبالعذر لا يكره السدل وهو أن يجعل الثوب على رأسه وكتفيه ويرسل جوانبه من غير أن يضمهما، وفي شرح الوقاية : هذا في الطيلسان)، أما في القباء) ونحوه فهو أن يلقيه على كتفيه من غير أن يدخل يديه في كميه انتهى، ولكن سنذكر عن الخلاصة» أن المختار عدم كراهته. وفي ( الظهيرية » : هو أن يضع ثوبه على كتفيـه ويـرســل طـرفيـه انتهى. وفي مجمع الروايات»: لو كان تحت الرداء قميص أو ثوب اختلفوا في كراهة السدل، والأصح أنه يكره انتهى. وفي ( البحر » عن «فتح القدير ) : أن السدل يصدق على أن يكون المنديل مرسلاً من كتفيه، كما يعتاده كثير، فينبغي لمن على عنقه منديل أن يضعه عند الصَّلاة، ولا فرق بين أن يكون الثوب محفوظاً عن الوقوع أو لا. انتهى. وذلك لقول أبي هريرة له عنـه أنـه عـلـيـه الصـلاة والسلام: «ن نَهَى عَنِ السَّدْلِ، وأنْ يُعْطِي الرَّجلُ فَاهُ ) رواه أبو داود والحاكم وصححه.
And it is disliked (Sadl). It is said: sada al-thawba sadlan, from the category of talab, and 'asdala' is a mistake, as in al-Diraya. Meaning: he lets his garment hang out of arrogance or carelessness, and with an excuse Sadl is not disliked. It is placing the garment on his head and shoulders and letting its sides hang without folding them. In Sharh al-Wiqaya: 'This is regarding the taylasan; as for the qaba' and the like, it is to throw it over his shoulders without inserting his hands into its sleeves.' End. But we will mention from al-Khulasa that the chosen opinion is that it is not disliked. And in al-Zuhayriyya: 'It is to place his garment on his shoulders and let its ends hang.' End. And in Majma' al-Riwayat: 'If there is a shirt or garment under the cloak, they disagreed about the dislike of Sadl, and the most correct is that it is disliked.' End. And in al-Bahr quoting Fath al-Qadir: 'Sadl applies to having a handkerchief hanging from his shoulders, as many do. So one who has a handkerchief on his neck should put it aside during prayer, regardless of whether the garment is secured from falling or not.' End. And that is due to the saying of Abu Huraira that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited Sadl and that a man should not cover his mouth. Narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim, and he authenticated it.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This is a ruling on Sadl, which is letting the outer garment (like a cloak or shawl) hang loosely from the shoulders without securing it. The author explains the definition: placing the garment on head and shoulders and letting the sides hang. He notes different applications: for a taylasan (a type of hooded cloak) and for a qaba' (a coat), and mentions that if one has an excuse (like cold), it is not disliked. There is disagreement among later scholars: some choose that it is not disliked at all, but the relied upon position is that it is makruh when done out of arrogance or carelessness. The proof is the hadith of Abu Huraira that the Prophet prohibited Sadl in prayer and also prohibited covering the mouth. The Hanafi ruling is that Sadl is makruh tanzihi if done without excuse; if done out of arrogance, it could be even more severe.

Key Terms
السَّدْلُ (al-sadl): Letting the outer garment (cloak, shawl, or handkerchief) hang from the shoulders loosely without folding or securing the sides.
الطيلسان (al-taylasān): A type of hooded cloak commonly worn on the head, like a hood, that is not wrapped around the neck.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the garment is made of silk.
B) When the person has an excuse (like cold).
C) When it is done in congregation.
D) When the garment is not a taylasan.

Key Takeaway
Sadl in prayer is makruh tanzihi if done without excuse; the hadith prohibition is relied upon, but the ruling accommodates valid needs.

Garment and Posture Makruhat in Salah
List of garment-related makruhat with proofs and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the disliked actions related to clothing and covering in salah, identify the hadith proof for ishtimal al-samma’, and explain the difference in ruling for sadl inside and outside prayer.

Core Idea
Wrapping the garment without an opening for the hands (al-ishtimal al-samma’) is makruh based on explicit hadith; other garment postures are disliked for resembling pride or non-believers.

In this lesson, we examine several makruhat (disliked actions) in salah that relate to how one wears their garment and covers their body. These actions are not invalidating but are discouraged for perfection. The strongest proof is the hadith prohibiting the ‘wrapping of the Jews,’ which the Hanafi school applies to any garment that leaves no opening for the hands. We also look at the cases of placing the garment under the armpit (sadl) and covering the mouth and nose (talaththum), and whether these rulings extend outside prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions and their ruling
List the specific actions described: ishtimal al-samma', talaththum, sadl, and placing garment under armpit. Each is ruled makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful).
Makruh tanzihi means leaving the recommended perfection, not prohibited.
2
Examine the dalil for ishtimal al-samma'
Read the hadith from Abu Dawud prohibiting the 'wrapping of the Jews.' Understand how the Hanafi school derives the dislike from this explicit prohibition.
The hadith is ahad but accepted; the dislike is based on the prohibition language.
3
Analyze the conditions and exceptions
Note the condition for ishtimal al-samma': no trousers required if done improperly; also the exception for sadl: not disliked outside prayer according to Abu Ja'far.
The ikhtilaf on sadl outside prayer shows the nuance in Hanafi ijtihad.
4
Connect to the principle of avoiding resemblance to non-believers
The text explains talaththum is disliked because it resembles fire worship. This principle of tashabbuh (imitation) is a key basis for many makruhat.
This principle is used in other chapters as well, e.g., clothing, greetings.

وتطويل الثانية على الأولى في جميع الصلواتِ، وتكرار السورةِ في ركعة واحدة من الفرض، وقراءة سورة فوق التي قرأها.
وقال الإمام أبو اليسر : لا يكره، وكذا في جامع المحبوبي»، لأن النوافل أمرها أسهل من الفرض، (و) يكره (تطويل الركعة ( الثَّانية على الركعة (الأولى) بثلاث آيات فأكثر، لا تطويل الثالثة لأنه ابتداء صلاةٍ، (في جَمِيعِ الصَّلَواتِ) أما الفرض فمتفق على الكراهة فيه، كما في « الخلاصة»، وأما النفل فيكره إطالة الثانية على الأولى في الأصح، إلحاقاً له بالفرض فيما لم يرد فيه تخصيص من التوسعة (وَ) يكره ( تكرارُ السُّورة في ركعةٍ واحدةٍ من الفرض ذكــره قـاضـي خــان»، وكذا تكرارها في ركعتين من الفرض إذا كان لغير ضرورة، بأن كان يقدر على قراءة سورة أخرى، أما إذا لم يقدر فلا يكره لوجوب ضم سورة إلى الفاتحة في الثانية أيضاً، وهذا إذا وقع عن قصد أما إذا كان لا عن قصد كما إذا قرأ قُلْ أَعُوذُ بِرَبِّ النَّاسِ) في الأولى فإنه لا يكره أن يكررها في الثانية، لأن قراءة سورة واحدة غير مكروه أي: في هذه الحالة، والقراءة منكوساً بأن يقرأ من البقرة مثلاً في هذه الحالة مكروه، بخلاف ما إذا ختم القرآن في الركعة الأولى، فإنه ينبغي أن يقرأ في الثانية بعد الفاتحة من البقرة؛ لأنا صرنا إليه بقول النبي : ( خَيْرُ النَّاسِ الحَالُ المرتحل ) يعني: الخاتم المفتتح، وكذا لا يكره لو أراد أن يقرأ غير التي قرأها في الأولى فافتتحها، فلما قرأ منها آية أو آيتين تذكر، فأراد أن يتركها ويفتح السورة التي أرادها يكره ذلك ؛ لقوله : ( إذا افْتَتَحْتَ سورةً فاقْرَأَهَا على نحوها » (٢) كذا في ( التجنيس والمزيد » ، ووجه الكراهة عدم وروده، ولم ينقل عن أحـد مـن السلف فعله في الفرض، فيكون بدعة ليس عليه أمره عليه الصلاة والسلام، فيكره في الفرض ولا يكره تكرار السورة في ركعة أو ركعتين من النفل، لأن باب التطوع أوسع، وقد ورد « أنه قام إلى الصَّباحُ بآيةٍ واحدةٍ، يكررها في تَهَجَدِهِ » (۳) فدل على جواز التكرار في التطوع، كذا في «شــرح المنية»، وقد ثبت عن جماعة من السلف أنهم كانوا يحيون ليلتهم بآية العذاب، أو آية الرحمة أو آية الرجاء، أو آية الخوف. وإن كان ذلك في الفرائض ، فهو مكروه إذ لم ينقل عن أحـد مـن السلف أنـه فعل مثل ذلك، كذا في ( التجنيس والمزيد)، (و) يكره (قراءة سورة فوق التي قرأها لما فيه من
And wrapping oneself in it such that he does not bring out his hands. And placing the garment under his right armpit, and throwing its two sides over his left shoulder... and recitation in other than the standing posture, and lengthening the first rak'ah in supererogatory prayer. In al-Muhit: because it resembles the action of the Jews during their fire worship, end. In al-Tabyin: it is disliked to cover the mouth and nose (talaththum) in prayer because it resembles the action of the Magians during their fire worship, end. The mashayikh differed regarding the dislike of letting the garment hang (sadl) outside prayer, and the correct is the statement of Abu Ja'far that it is not disliked, as in al-Bughyah and al-Bahr, from al-Qunyah. And it is disliked to wrap oneself in the garment such that he does not leave an opening to bring out his hands, which is al-ishtimal al-samma', due to what Abu Dawud narrated from Ibn 'Umar: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said, 'When one of you has two garments, let him pray in them; if he has only one garment, let him tie it as a wrapper (izar) and not wrap it like the wrapping of the Jews.' It is called so because there is no opening to bring out his hand like a solid rock. And in al-Muhit it is interpreted as gathering the two ends of his garment and bringing them out from under one hand over one shoulder, and in al-Bada'i it is conditioned that he should not be wearing trousers because then exposure of the private parts is not feared. And it is disliked to place the garment under the right armpit and throw its two sides over the left shoulder or vice versa, because covering the shoulders in prayer is recommended (mustahabb), so leaving it without necessity is makruh tanzihi. And in Sharh al-Munyah: it is disliked for the one praying to do anything that is from the characteristics of tyrants generally, because prayer is a station of humility, lowliness, and submissiveness, and it is incompatible with pride and arrogance. And it is disliked to recite in other than the standing posture, such as completing recitation while bowing, and it is disliked to perform the prescribed remembrances (adhkar) during transitions after completing the transition, because it involves two faults: leaving it in its proper place and performing it elsewhere. And it is disliked to lengthen the first rak'ah in every pair of supererogatory prayer, as in al-Muhit, unless that lengthening is reported from the Prophet or from one of the Companions, such as reciting 'Alif Lam Mim' (Surah al-Sajdah) and 'Hal ata' (Surah al-Insan) and 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad' (Surah al-Ikhlas) in witr, for in terms of recitation it is annexed to supererogatory prayers. (Note: all this applies when there is no excuse and no pride; if due to an excuse without pride, then no dislike at all; if with an excuse but with pride, or for pride only, it is disliked absolutely.) And lengthening the second rak'ah over the first in all prayers, and repeating a surah in one rak'ah of obligatory (fard) prayer, and reciting a surah after the one he recited. Imam Abu al-Yusr said: it is not disliked, as in Jami' al-Mahbubi, because supererogatory prayers are easier than obligatory. And it is disliked to lengthen the second rak'ah over the first by three or more verses, not lengthening the third because it is the beginning of a prayer, in all prayers. As for fard, there is agreement on its dislike, as in al-Khulasa; as for nafl, it is disliked to lengthen the second over the first in the correct opinion, by analogizing it to fard in matters where no specific leniency is reported. And it is disliked to repeat a surah in one rak'ah of fard, mentioned by Qadi Khan, and likewise repeating it in two rak'ahs of fard if without necessity, such that he is able to read another surah; but if he is unable, then it is not disliked because it is obligatory to join a surah to al-Fatiha in the second as well. This applies if done intentionally; if unintentionally, such as if he recited 'Qul A'udhu bi Rabbi al-Nas' (Surah al-Nas) in the first, then it is not disliked to repeat it in the second, because reciting one surah is not disliked in this case. And reciting in reverse order (mankusan), such as reciting from al-Baqarah in this case [after having recited a later surah], is disliked, contrary to if he completed the Quran in the first rak'ah; then he should recite in the second after al-Fatiha from al-Baqarah, because we adhere to the Prophet's saying: 'The best of people is the one who finishes and begins anew,' meaning the one who completes and starts. Likewise, it is not disliked if he intends to recite a surah different from the one he recited in the first and starts it, but after reciting one or two verses he remembers and wants to leave it and start the surah he intended; this is disliked because of his saying: 'When you start a surah, recite it through to its end.' The basis of dislike is its lack of precedent; it is not transmitted from any of the Salaf doing it in fard, so it is an innovation without the order of the Prophet (peace be upon him), thus disliked in fard. But repeating a surah in one or two rak'ahs of nafl is not disliked, because the realm of supererogatory is broader, and it is reported that 'he stood for the whole night with one verse, repeating it in his tahajjud,' indicating permissibility of repetition in nafl. It is also confirmed from a group of the Salaf that they would spend their night with a verse of punishment, mercy, hope, or fear. If that were in the obligatory prayers, it would be disliked, as it is not transmitted from any of the Salaf that they did such. And it is disliked to recite a surah after the one he recited [i.e., to skip a surah and recite a later one before the earlier] because of what it contains of
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is an expansion (sharh) on the matn of Nur al-Idah, listing various disliked actions (makruhat) in salah. The author details each ruling with proofs and explanations, distinguishing between obligatory (fard) and supererogatory (nafl) prayers, and noting conditions. The passage begins with the dislike of wrapping oneself in a garment such that hands cannot be brought out (al-ishtimal al-samma'), citing a hadith from Abu Dawud prohibiting imitation of Jewish practice. It also covers placing the garment under the armpit and over the shoulder (sadl) as makruh tanzihi, as it resembles the behavior of tyrants and contradicts the humility of prayer. Recitation in non-standing postures (e.g., finishing recitation while bowing) is disliked because it moves the dhikr from its proper place. Lengthening the first rak'ah of nafl prayer over the second is generally disliked unless it follows a reported practice from the Prophet or Companions. The text then addresses lengthening the second rak'ah over the first: while agreed upon as makruh in fard, in nafl there is a difference; the correct view (al-ashah) is that it is also disliked by analogy to fard. Repetition of a surah in a single rak'ah of fard is disliked if intentional and avoidable, but not in nafl due to broader scope; the author cites a hadith about the Prophet repeating a verse in tahajjud. Reciting surahs in reverse order (mankus) is also disliked. The passage ends with the dislike of reciting a surah after the one he had already recited (i.e., skipping an intermediate surah). The commentary consistently anchors rulings in transmitted precedent and avoids innovation.

Key Terms
اشتمالة الصماء (al-ishtimal al-samma'): Wrapping the garment around the body without leaving an opening for the hands, resembling a solid rock.
السدل (al-sadl): Placing the garment under the armpit and throwing it over the shoulder, leaving hands free.
التلثم (al-talaththum): Covering the mouth and nose during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the dislike of al-ishtimal al-samma' in prayer?
A) Qiyas on the practice of Magians
B) Hadith from Abu Dawud forbidding the 'wrapping of the Jews'
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) General principle of avoiding pride

Key Takeaway
Garment and posture makruhat in salah are based on explicit hadith and the principle of tashabbuh, and they do not invalidate prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Recitation and Sequence Makruhat in Salah
List of recitation and sequence makruhat with proofs and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the disliked actions related to recitation timing, lengthening rak'ahs, repeating surahs, and reverse order in prayer, and apply the principle of avoiding innovation.

Core Idea
Recitation should be in its proper posture; lengthening rak'ahs in a non-Sunnah manner and repeating surahs in fard is makruh due to lack of precedent.

This lesson covers the makruhat associated with how and when we recite during prayer, as well as the sequence and length of rak'ahs. The Hanafi school stresses that recitation should be performed in the standing posture, and that any deviation from the transmitted practice of the Salaf in fard prayers is disliked. However, in supererogatory prayers (nafl), there is more flexibility, as evidenced by the Prophet's practice of repeating a single verse all night. We also examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on lengthening the second rak'ah over the first in nafl.

Guided Path
1
List the recitation-related makruhat
Identify: reading in non-standing posture (e.g., completing recitation while bowing), performing dhikr after the transition, lengthening first rak'ah in nafl, lengthening second rak'ah over first in both fard and nafl, repeating a surah in one or two rak'ahs of fard, reading in reverse order, and reading a surah after the one already recited (skipping).
Each has a specific basis; note exceptions like the Witr recitation of specific surahs.
2
Analyze the basis for each ruling
For reading in non-standing: it moves the dhikr from its proper place. For lengthening: it is an innovation unless reported from the Prophet or Sahabah. For repeating surah in fard: it was not done by Salaf and thus bid'ah. For reverse order: likewise.
The key principle is 'kullu dhikr fat mahallahu la yu'ta bihi fi ghayrihi' (every remembrance that misses its place is not performed elsewhere).
3
Distinguish between fard and nafl
Many of these makruhat apply strictly to fard prayers; in nafl, the ruling is more lenient. For example, repeating a surah is not disliked in nafl; lengthening second rak'ah over first is disagreed upon in nafl.
The Prophet's practice of repeating a verse all night in tahajjud is evidence for leniency in nafl.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
On lengthening the second rak'ah over the first in nafl: Imam Abu al-Yusr said it is not disliked, while the majority (al-ashah) say it is disliked by analogy to fard.
The mufta bihi is the majority view of dislike.

And wrapping oneself in it such that he does not bring out his hands. And placing the garment under his right armpit, and throwing its two sides over his left shoulder... and recitation in other than the standing posture, and lengthening the first rak'ah in supererogatory prayer. In al-Muhit: because it resembles the action of the Jews during their fire worship, end. In al-Tabyin: it is disliked to cover the mouth and nose (talaththum) in prayer because it resembles the action of the Magians during their fire worship, end. The mashayikh differed regarding the dislike of letting the garment hang (sadl) outside prayer, and the correct is the statement of Abu Ja'far that it is not disliked, as in al-Bughyah and al-Bahr, from al-Qunyah. And it is disliked to wrap oneself in the garment such that he does not leave an opening to bring out his hands, which is al-ishtimal al-samma', due to what Abu Dawud narrated from Ibn 'Umar: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said, 'When one of you has two garments, let him pray in them; if he has only one garment, let him tie it as a wrapper (izar) and not wrap it like the wrapping of the Jews.' It is called so because there is no opening to bring out his hand like a solid rock. And in al-Muhit it is interpreted as gathering the two ends of his garment and bringing them out from under one hand over one shoulder, and in al-Bada'i it is conditioned that he should not be wearing trousers because then exposure of the private parts is not feared. And it is disliked to place the garment under the right armpit and throw its two sides over the left shoulder or vice versa, because covering the shoulders in prayer is recommended (mustahabb), so leaving it without necessity is makruh tanzihi. And in Sharh al-Munyah: it is disliked for the one praying to do anything that is from the characteristics of tyrants generally, because prayer is a station of humility, lowliness, and submissiveness, and it is incompatible with pride and arrogance. And it is disliked to recite in other than the standing posture, such as completing recitation while bowing, and it is disliked to perform the prescribed remembrances (adhkar) during transitions after completing the transition, because it involves two faults: leaving it in its proper place and performing it elsewhere. And it is disliked to lengthen the first rak'ah in every pair of supererogatory prayer, as in al-Muhit, unless that lengthening is reported from the Prophet or from one of the Companions, such as reciting 'Alif Lam Mim' (Surah al-Sajdah) and 'Hal ata' (Surah al-Insan) and 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad' (Surah al-Ikhlas) in witr, for in terms of recitation it is annexed to supererogatory prayers. (Note: all this applies when there is no excuse and no pride; if due to an excuse without pride, then no dislike at all; if with an excuse but with pride, or for pride only, it is disliked absolutely.) And lengthening the second rak'ah over the first in all prayers, and repeating a surah in one rak'ah of obligatory (fard) prayer, and reciting a surah after the one he recited. Imam Abu al-Yusr said: it is not disliked, as in Jami' al-Mahbubi, because supererogatory prayers are easier than obligatory. And it is disliked to lengthen the second rak'ah over the first by three or more verses, not lengthening the third because it is the beginning of a prayer, in all prayers. As for fard, there is agreement on its dislike, as in al-Khulasa; as for nafl, it is disliked to lengthen the second over the first in the correct opinion, by analogizing it to fard in matters where no specific leniency is reported. And it is disliked to repeat a surah in one rak'ah of fard, mentioned by Qadi Khan, and likewise repeating it in two rak'ahs of fard if without necessity, such that he is able to read another surah; but if he is unable, then it is not disliked because it is obligatory to join a surah to al-Fatiha in the second as well. This applies if done intentionally; if unintentionally, such as if he recited 'Qul A'udhu bi Rabbi al-Nas' (Surah al-Nas) in the first, then it is not disliked to repeat it in the second, because reciting one surah is not disliked in this case. And reciting in reverse order (mankusan), such as reciting from al-Baqarah in this case [after having recited a later surah], is disliked, contrary to if he completed the Quran in the first rak'ah; then he should recite in the second after al-Fatiha from al-Baqarah, because we adhere to the Prophet's saying: 'The best of people is the one who finishes and begins anew,' meaning the one who completes and starts. Likewise, it is not disliked if he intends to recite a surah different from the one he recited in the first and starts it, but after reciting one or two verses he remembers and wants to leave it and start the surah he intended; this is disliked because of his saying: 'When you start a surah, recite it through to its end.' The basis of dislike is its lack of precedent; it is not transmitted from any of the Salaf doing it in fard, so it is an innovation without the order of the Prophet (peace be upon him), thus disliked in fard. But repeating a surah in one or two rak'ahs of nafl is not disliked, because the realm of supererogatory is broader, and it is reported that 'he stood for the whole night with one verse, repeating it in his tahajjud,' indicating permissibility of repetition in nafl. It is also confirmed from a group of the Salaf that they would spend their night with a verse of punishment, mercy, hope, or fear. If that were in the obligatory prayers, it would be disliked, as it is not transmitted from any of the Salaf that they did such. And it is disliked to recite a surah after the one he recited [i.e., to skip a surah and recite a later one before the earlier] because of what it contains of

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is an expansion (sharh) on the matn of Nur al-Idah, listing various disliked actions (makruhat) in salah. The author details each ruling with proofs and explanations, distinguishing between obligatory (fard) and supererogatory (nafl) prayers, and noting conditions. The passage begins with the dislike of wrapping oneself in a garment such that hands cannot be brought out (al-ishtimal al-samma'), citing a hadith from Abu Dawud prohibiting imitation of Jewish practice. It also covers placing the garment under the armpit and over the shoulder (sadl) as makruh tanzihi, as it resembles the behavior of tyrants and contradicts the humility of prayer. Recitation in non-standing postures (e.g., finishing recitation while bowing) is disliked because it moves the dhikr from its proper place. Lengthening the first rak'ah of nafl prayer over the second is generally disliked unless it follows a reported practice from the Prophet or Companions. The text then addresses lengthening the second rak'ah over the first: while agreed upon as makruh in fard, in nafl there is a difference; the correct view (al-ashah) is that it is also disliked by analogy to fard. Repetition of a surah in a single rak'ah of fard is disliked if intentional and avoidable, but not in nafl due to broader scope; the author cites a hadith about the Prophet repeating a verse in tahajjud. Reciting surahs in reverse order (mankus) is also disliked. The passage ends with the dislike of reciting a surah after the one he had already recited (i.e., skipping an intermediate surah). The commentary consistently anchors rulings in transmitted precedent and avoids innovation.

Key Terms
الاندراج (al-indiraj): Wrapping the garment tightly around the body.
القراءة منكوساً (al-qira'ah mankusan): Reciting surahs in reverse order (e.g., reciting a later surah before an earlier one).
تكرار السورة (tikrar al-surah): Repeating the same surah in the same or different rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid and not disliked
B) Valid but makruh tanzihi
C) Invalid because it is an innovation
D) Makruh tahrimi (prohibited)

Key Takeaway
Recitation and sequence makruhat stem from the need to follow the transmitted practice of the Salaf; fard is stricter, nafl is more lenient.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Lengthening the Second Rak'ah Over the First: Ruling and Dispute
Ruling on prolonging the second rak'ah more than the first in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on lengthening the second rak'ah over the first and identify the threshold that triggers dislike.

Core Idea
Lengthening the second rak'ah over the first is makruh if the excess is three verses, whether in fard or nafl.

In prayer, the recommended practice is to make the first rak'ah longer in recitation than the second. Deliberately reversing this order by a significant amount raises a question: is it permissible or disliked? This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on this issue, including an intra-madhhab dispute and the precise threshold for dislike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act in question is lengthening the second rak'ah over the first in any prayer. The ruling according to the relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is makruh tanzih (disliked).
Makruh tanzih means it is better to avoid, but not sinful.
2
Note the Threshold
The dislike is specifically triggered when the second rak'ah is made longer by three verses or more. A smaller difference is not considered disliked.
This threshold reflects a significant deviation from the recommended practice.
3
Recognize the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Imam Abu al-Yusr (a Hanafi scholar) held that it is not disliked, citing the ease of supererogatory prayers. However, the majority, including the commentator of Nur al-Idah, maintain the dislike.
This dispute is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the Proof (Dalil)
The ruling is based on qiyas (analogy) to fard prayers, where there is consensus on dislike, and no specific concession for nawafil is reported. Thus, the analogy is applied uniformly.
Qiyas is a valid but zanni (speculative) proof, hence the ruling is makruh, not haram.
5
Distinguish Fard vs Nafl and Exception for Third Rak'ah
For fard prayers, the dislike is agreed upon. For nafl, the majority still holds dislike. Lengthening the third rak'ah over the first is not disliked, because the third starts a new pair.
The exception for the third rak'ah clarifies that the ruling only applies to the second relative to the first within a pair.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتطويل الثانية على الأولى في جميع الصلواتِ.
وقال الإمام أبو اليسر : لا يكره، وكذا في جامع المحبوبي» لأن النوافل أمرها أسهل من الفرض، (و) يكره (تطويل الركعة ( الثَّانية على الركعة (الأولى) بثلاث آيات فأكثر، لا تطويل الثالثة لأنه ابتداء صلاةٍ، (في جَمِيعِ الصَّلَواتِ) أما الفرض فمتفق على الكراهة فيه، كما في « الخلاصة»، وأما النفل فيكره إطالة الثانية على الأولى في الأصح، إلحاقاً له بالفرض فيما لم يرد فيه تخصيص من التوسعة
And lengthening the second over the first in all prayers. And Imam Abu al-Yusr said: it is not disliked, and similarly in Jami' al-Mahbubi, because supererogatory acts are easier than obligatory. And it is disliked to lengthen the second rak'ah over the first by three verses or more, not lengthening the third because it is the beginning of a prayer, in all prayers. As for obligatory, there is agreement on its dislike as in al-Khulasa. As for supererogatory, it is disliked to lengthen the second over the first according to the most correct opinion, by analogy to obligatory where no specific concession has been reported.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on making the second rak'ah longer than the first in prayer. The matn states it is disliked in all prayers. The commentary first notes a difference of opinion: Imam Abu al-Yusr holds it is not disliked, citing the ease of nawafil. However, the relied-upon position is that it is disliked (makruh) for both fard and nafl when the excess is three or more verses. Lengthening the third rak'ah is not disliked because it is the beginning of a new prayer pair. For fard prayers, there is consensus on the dislike. For nafl, the preferred view is that it is also disliked, by analogy to fard, as no specific relaxation is reported.

Key Terms
تطويل (tatwil): Making one rak'ah longer in recitation than another
توسعة (tawsi'ah): Concession or relaxation in the ruling
كراهة (karahah): Dislike, a ruling that is better to avoid but not sinful

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the threshold for considering the lengthening of the second rak'ah over the first as disliked?
A) One verse
B) Two verses
C) Three verses or more
D) Any difference

Key Takeaway
Lengthening the second rak'ah over the first is makruh tanzih if the excess is three verses or more, based on analogy to fard, with a minority view permitting it for nawafil.

Repeating a Surah in One Rak'ah of Fard
Ruling on repeating a surah in one rak'ah of obligatory prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeating a surah in fard prayers, identify the exceptions (necessity, unintentional), and distinguish the ruling for nafl.

Core Idea
Repeating a surah in fard is disliked unless necessary; in nafl it is permissible.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on repeating a surah within a single rak'ah or across two rak'ahs of fard prayers. We will analyze the conditions under which repetition is disliked, the exceptions for necessity and unintentional repetition, and the general permissibility in nafl. The proofs from hadith and the reasoning of the salaf will be explored.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling
Identify the ruling on repeating a surah in one rak'ah of fard as stated in the matn: it is makruh (disliked).
The same ruling applies to repeating a surah in two rak'ahs of fard.
2
Identify the exceptions
Note the conditions that remove the dislike: if the person is unable to recite another surah (necessity) or if the repetition is unintentional (e.g., forgetting).
Inability includes not knowing another surah or forgetting.
3
Analyze the proofs
Examine the hadith quoted: 'The best of people are those who complete and begin' and 'When you begin a surah, recite it in full.' Understand how these support the dislike of abandoning a surah and maintaining order.
The hadith are general; the dislike is derived from lack of practice among the salaf.
4
Compare fard vs nafl
Observe that in nafl (voluntary prayers), repeating a surah is not disliked, based on reports of the Prophet and salaf repeating verses in tahajjud.
The door of voluntary worship is wider.
5
Consider related rulings
Note the rulings on reciting in reverse order (mankus) and abandoning a surah once started—both are disliked in fard.
These follow from the same principle of avoiding innovation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتكرار السورةِ في ركعة واحدة من الفرض.
و) يكره ( تكرارُ السُّورة في ركعةٍ واحدةٍ من الفرض ذكــره قـاضـي خــان»، وكذا تكرارها في ركعتين من الفرض إذا كان لغير ضرورة، بأن كان يقدر على قراءة سورة أخرى، أما إذا لم يقدر فلا يكره لوجوب ضم سورة إلى الفاتحة في الثانية أيضاً، وهذا إذا وقع عن قصد أما إذا كان لا عن قصد كما إذا قرأ قُلْ أَعُوذُ بِرَبِّ النَّاسِ) في الأولى فإنه لا يكره أن يكررها في الثانية، لأن قراءة سورة واحدة غير مكروه أي: في هذه الحالة، والقراءة منكوساً بأن يقرأ من البقرة مثلاً في هذه الحالة مكروه، بخلاف ما إذا ختم القرآن في الركعة الأولى، فإنه ينبغي أن يقرأ في الثانية بعد الفاتحة من البقرة؛ لأنا صرنا إليه بقول النبي : ( خَيْرُ النَّاسِ الحَالُ المرتحل ) يعني: الخاتم المفتتح، وكذا لا يكره لو أراد أن يقرأ غير التي قرأها في الأولى فافتتحها، فلما قرأ منها آية أو آيتين تذكر، فأراد أن يتركها ويفتح السورة التي أرادها يكره ذلك ؛ لقوله : ( إذا افْتَتَحْتَ سورةً فاقْرَأَهَا على نحوها » (٢) كذا في ( التجنيس والمزيد » ، ووجه الكراهة عدم وروده، ولم ينقل عن أحـد مـن السلف فعله في الفرض، فيكون بدعة ليس عليه أمره عليه الصلاة والسلام، فيكره في الفرض ولا يكره تكرار السورة في ركعة أو ركعتين من النفل، لأن باب التطوع أوسع، وقد ورد « أنه قام إلى الصَّباحُ بآيةٍ واحدةٍ، يكررها في تَهَجَدِهِ » (۳) فدل على جواز التكرار في التطوع، كذا في «شــرح المنية»، وقد ثبت عن جماعة من السلف أنهم كانوا يحيون ليلتهم بآية العذاب، أو آية الرحمة أو آية الرجاء، أو آية الخوف. وإن كان ذلك في الفرائض ، فهو مكروه إذ لم ينقل عن أحـد مـن السلف أنـه فعل مثل ذلك، كذا في ( التجنيس والمزيد)،
And repeating the surah in one rak'ah of fard. And it is disliked: repeating the surah in one rak'ah of fard, as mentioned by Qadi Khan, and similarly repeating it in two rak'ahs of fard if without necessity, such that he is able to read another surah; but if he is unable, it is not disliked because it is obligatory to add a surah to the Fatiha in the second also. This applies when done intentionally; if unintentionally, as when he recited 'Say: I seek refuge with the Lord of mankind' in the first, it is not disliked to repeat it in the second, because reciting one surah is not disliked in this case. And reciting in reverse order, e.g., reciting from al-Baqarah, is disliked in such a case. Contrary to if he completed the Quran in the first rak'ah; then he should recite after the Fatiha from al-Baqarah in the second, because we follow the Prophet's saying: 'The best of people are those who complete and begin.' Similarly, it is not disliked if he intended to read another surah than the one he read in the first, then started it, and after reciting one or two verses remembered, and wanted to leave it and open the surah he intended; that is disliked because of his saying: 'When you begin a surah, recite it in full.' The reason for dislike is its lack of transmission, and no salaf is reported to have done it in fard, so it is an innovation. It is disliked in fard but not disliked in nafl in one or two rak'ahs, because the door of voluntary acts is wider. And it is reported that he stood until morning with one verse, repeating it in his tahajjud, indicating permissibility in supererogatory acts. This is in Sharh al-Munya. And it is established that a group of salaf used to spend their night reciting a verse of punishment, mercy, hope, or fear. If that were in fard, it would be disliked, as no salaf is reported to have done that.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on repeating a surah in prayer. The matn states it is disliked to repeat a surah in one rak'ah of fard. The commentary expands: repeating a surah in one or two rak'ahs of fard is disliked unless there is a necessity (e.g., inability to recite another surah). If intentional, it is disliked; if unintentional (like forgetting and repeating), it is not. The commentary also addresses reciting in reverse order (like reading a later surah before an earlier one) as disliked. A special case: if a person has completed the entire Quran in the first rak'ah, in the second he should start from al-Baqarah, following the hadith 'the best of people are those who complete and begin.' Starting a surah and then abandoning it is disliked. The underlying reason for dislike in fard is that it is not transmitted from the salaf, hence deemed an innovation. However, in nafl (supererogatory prayers), repetition is permissible and even reported from the Prophet (ﷺ) and the salaf, as the rules are more lenient.

Key Terms
تكرار السورة (takrar al-surah): Reciting the same surah more than once within a rak'ah or across rak'ahs
القراءة منكوساً (al-qira'ah mankusan): Reciting surahs in reverse order (e.g., later surah before earlier)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is repeating a surah in two rak'ahs of fard not disliked according to this passage?
A) When the person intends to repeat
B) When unable to recite another surah
C) When it is a long surah
D) When it is the last rak'ah

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, repeating a surah in fard is makruh unless necessitated by inability to recite another surah; in nafl, it is permissible.

Makruhat of Salah: Disliked Actions and Their Basis
List of disliked actions in salah with brief evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the disliked actions in salah mentioned in the passage and explain why each is considered makruh tanzihi according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Various actions during salah are makruh because they contradict khushu' or the sunnah, though they do not invalidate the prayer.

This lesson examines a section from Imdad al-Fattah that enumerates several actions disliked in salah. The rulings are based on the principle of preserving devotion and following the prophetic model. We will explore each action and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify each makruh action
List the actions mentioned: extra surah between two surahs, smelling perfume, fanning once or twice, turning fingers or feet from qibla, leaving hands from knees in ruku', yawning, closing eyes, raising eyes to the sky, stretching, minor actions, taking/killing a louse.
All are considered makruh tanzihi unless otherwise specified.
2
Understand the reason for dislike
For each action, note why it detracts from khushu' or contradicts the sunnah. For example, yawning is associated with laziness and Satan; closing eyes prevents khushu' unless needed; fanning introduces extraneous movement.
The common theme is lack of devotion and focus.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on lice
Abu Hanifa preferred burying the louse, Muhammad allowed killing, and Abu Yusuf considered both makruh. The relied-upon position is that such actions are makruh unless there is an excuse.
This shows the scope of scholarly discussion within the school.
4
Apply the ruling category
All these actions are makruh tanzihi – disliked but not sinful. They do not invalidate the prayer, but avoiding them completes its perfection.
Repeated or excessive minor actions may border on makruh tahrimi or invalidate if they become habitual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفَضْلُهُ بسُورةِ بينَ سُورتين قرأهما في ركعتين. وشَمَّ طِيبِ، وَتَرْوِيحُهُ بثوبِهِ، أَوْ مِرْوَحَةٍ، مَرَّةً، أو مرتين، وتحويل أصابع يديه، أو رجليه، عن القبلة، في السجودِ، وغيرهِ وتَرْكُ وضع اليدين على الركبتين في الركوع. والتثاؤب . . . وتغميضُ عَيْنَيْهِ، ورَفْعُهُمَا للسّماء، والتَّمَطَّي، والعملُ القليلُ، وأَخذُ قَمْلَةٍ، وقَتْلُها ..
And disliking [reading] an extra surah between two surahs read in two rak'ahs. And smelling perfume, and fanning himself with his garment or a fan once or twice, and turning his fingers or feet away from the qibla in prostration and elsewhere, and leaving placing the hands on the knees in bowing. And yawning... and closing his eyes, and raising them to the sky, and stretching, and minor actions, and taking a louse and killing it...
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah lists several makruh (disliked) actions during prayer. The author begins with recitation: it is makruh to recite an extra surah between two surahs already recited in two rak'ahs, as it resembles preferring some parts of the Quran over others. Smelling perfume intentionally is makruh because it is extraneous to prayer; if the scent enters unintentionally, it is not disliked. Fanning oneself once or twice is makruh for lacking khushu'. Turning fingers or feet away from the qibla during prostration or other postures contradicts the sunnah of orienting limbs toward the qibla. Not placing hands on knees in ruku' is makruh because it abandons a sunnah. Yawning is disliked as it indicates laziness; the hadith instructs to suppress it or cover the mouth. Closing the eyes is makruh tanzihan unless necessary to maintain khushu'. Raising eyes to the sky is prohibited by a hadith threatening loss of sight. Stretching (tamattu) is disliked for opposing khushu'. Minor actions like plucking a hair or taking a louse are makruh, with some ikhtilaf among the imams regarding killing lice: Abu Hanifa preferred burying, Muhammad allowed killing, Abu Yusuf considered both makruh.

Key Terms
تثاؤب (tathā'ub): Yawning during prayer, which is disliked due to its association with laziness and Satan.
تمطي (tamattī): Stretching the body intentionally during prayer, disliked as it distracts from khushu'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it breaks wudu
B) Because it is from Satan and indicates laziness
C) Because it invalidates the prayer
D) Because it is prohibited by Quran

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school regards these actions as makruh tanzihi to preserve the spirit of devotion in salah.

Disliked Actions: Eyes and Stretching in Prayer
Rulings with proofs and exception for closing eyes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on closing and raising eyes during prayer and explain the reasoning and exceptions.

Core Idea
Closing or raising eyes during prayer compromises khushu'; it is makruh tanzihi unless necessary.

Prayer is a state of humble devotion (khushu'), and certain actions contradict that spirit. The Hanafi school identifies several disliked acts (makruhat) to help preserve the sanctity of salah. In this lesson, we examine three related to the eyes and body: closing the eyes, raising them to the sky, and stretching lazily. We will explore the proofs, the reasoning, and the important exception when closing the eyes actually aids concentration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions and their ruling
From the matn we see: closing eyes, raising eyes, and stretching are listed as makruh. The commentary confirms the ruling is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful) unless there is a reason.
Makruh tanzihi means it is better to avoid but the act remains valid.
2
Locate the proofs (hadith)
For raising eyes: the hadith 'Let them desist or their eyesight will be snatched away' (Bukhari). For closing eyes: the hadith 'When one of you stands in prayer, let him not close his eyes' (weaker authority).
Hanafis consider the hadith on raising eyes stronger (sahih).
3
Understand the reasoning (illah)
The ruling is based on contradicting khushu', appearing lazy or frivolous, and for closing eyes, missing the sunnah of looking at the place of prostration.
Khushu' is the essence of prayer.
4
Note the exception for closing eyes
If closing the eyes helps maintain khushu' by blocking distracting sights, it becomes not only permissible but preferable.
This exception is from al-Bahr and is accepted in the school.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a person prays in a busy area and can't concentrate, closing the eyes is recommendable. Otherwise, it is disliked.
The default is to keep eyes open and focus on the place of sujud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتغميض عَيْنَيْهِ، ورَفْعُهُمَا للسّماء، والتَّمَطَّي، والعملُ القليلُ، وأَخذُ قَمْلَةٍ، وقَتْلُها .. و « التبيين»، وقال في « البحر ) : وضع اليد ثابت في مسلم والكم قياس، وفي «الخلاصة»: إن أمكنه أخذ شفتيه بسنه فليفعل، ويضع ظهر يده على فيه، كما في «مختارات النوازل»، ويكون بيمينه، وقيل: في القيام بها وفي غيره بيساره، كذا في المجتبى»، (وَ) يكره (تغميضُ عَيْنَيْهِ) لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( إذَا قَامَ أحَدُكُمْ في الصَّلاةِ فَلا يُغْمِضُ عَيْنَيْهِ ، [ ولأنه ينافي ] الخشوع، وفيه نوع عبث، وترك النظر إلى الموضع المسنون، ولأن كل عضو وطرف ذو حظ من هذه العبادة، فكذا العين، وينبغي أن تكون الكراهة تنزيهية إذا كان لغير ضرورة و [ لا ] مصلحة، أما لو خــاف فـوت الخشوع بسبب رؤية ما يفوق الخاطر فلا يكره غمضهما، بل ربما يكون أولى، لأنه حينئذ كمال للخشوع قاله صاحب البحر » . (و) يكره (رَفْعُهُما للسّماء) لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: « مَا بَالُ أقْوَامٍ يَرْفَعُونَ أَبْصَارَهُمْ إلى السَّمَاءِ لِيَنْتَهِين أو لتُخطفَنَّ أبصارهم ) كذا في ( البرهان»، (والتَّمَطي)) لأنه من التكاسل، وهو ينافي الخشوع. (و) يكره ( العملُ القليلُ) المنافي للصلاة، وأفراده كثيرة كنتف شعرة، أو شعرتين، وتقدم الفــرق بين العمل القليل والكثير، وجعل منه قاضي خان الرمية الواحدة عن القوس في صلاة الخوف ولا تقام إلا باليدين، ولعله لأن في تلك الحالة لا يظن به أنه ليس في الصلاة، لما أنـه لمـا أبـيـح لـه المشي، فكذا الرمية لاحتياجه إليها، (وَ) منه (أَخْذُ قَمْلَةٍ، وقَتْلُها ) من غير عذر، إذ لو شغلته أو شغله برغوث بالعض لا يكره الأخذ، وفي مجمع الروايات»: ويكره أن يأخذ قملة ويقتلها، لكن يدفنها تحت الحصى، وفي قول أبي حنيفة وروي عنه إن أخذ قملة أو دفنها فقد أساء انتهى. وفي « البزازية » : قال الإمام: دفنها فيها أحب من قتلها، وقال محمد قتلها، وقال الثاني: كلاهما مكروه انتهى.
وتغطية أنفه، وفمه. وفي « التجنيس : وعن محمد رحمه الله : أن قتل القملة في الصلاة أحب إلي من دفنها، وكـل ذلك لا بأس به، قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله : لا يقتل القملة في الصلاة ويدفنها تحت الحصى، لما روي عبد الله بن مسعود الله أنه كان يصلي فأخذ قملة ودفنها، ثم تلا قوله تعالى: ﴿أَلَمْ تَجَعَلِ الْأَرْضَ كفانا (١) [ المرسلات : ٢٥] ووجه القتل أن فيه إزالة الأذى عن نفسه، فلا يكون بـه بـأس، كقتل الحية والعقرب انتهى. وقال في ( التجنيس ) : أيضاً الكف عن قتل القملة أفضل. انتهى، قلت: ووجهـه لمـا فيه من ترك العمل والاحتراز عن النجاسة المختلفة فيها، قال الجلال السيوطي في « الينبوع » : قــال الزركشي كره مالك رحمه الله تعالى قتل البراغيث والقمل في المسجد، وصرح النووي بأنه إذا قتلها لا يجوز إلقاؤها في المسجد لأنها ميتة، وفي مسند أحمد عن أبي أيوب قال: « وَجَدَ رَجُلٌ في ثَوْبِهِ قَمْلَةٌ فَأَخَذَهَا فَطَرَحَهَا فِي المَسْجِدْ، فَقَالَ لَهُ رَسُولُ الله : « لا تَفْعَلْ رُدَّهَا فِي ثَوْبِكَ حَتَّى تَخْرُجَ مِنَ المَسْجِدِ » (۳) وقال ابن العماد: وأما طرح القمل في المسجد فإن كان ميتــا حــرم لنجاسته، وإن كان حياً ففي كتب المالكية أنه يحرم طرح القمل حياً بخلاف البرغوث، والفرق أن البرغوث يعيش بأكل التراب، بخلاف القمل ففي طرحه تعذيب له بالجوع وهو لا يجوز، وقـد قـال : «إِنَّ اللَّهَ كَتَبَ الإِحْسَانَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ فَإِذَا قَتَلْتُمْ فَأَحْسِنُوا الْقِتْلَةَ ", وعلى هذا فيحرم طرح الــمــل حـيـاً في المسجد وغيره، ويحرم على الرجل أن يلقي ثيابه وفيها قمل قبل قتله، والأولى أن لا يقتله في المسجد. لحديث: « إِذَا وَجَدَ أَحَدُكُمْ الْقَمْلَةَ فِي ثَوْبِهِ فَلْيَصُرَّهَا وَلا يَطْرَحُهَا فِي الْمَسْجِدِ » ) رواه أحمد. ولو قتل القمل في ثيابه وتركه فيها ميتاً وصلى فيها لم تصح صلاته، لأن ميتة القمل والبرغوث نجسان على الصحيح خلافاً للقفال » ، ويعفى عن قليل دمها في الثوب، وإن تعمد قتلها بخلاف الجلد فإنه لا مشقة في التحرز منه ولو حصل على حصر المسجد دم البراغيث ممن ينام في المسجد ففي العفو عنه بالنسبة إلى المصلي نظراً، لأن التحرز عنه ممكن، وينبغي أن يؤمر النائم بأن يجعل بينه وبين الحصير حائلاً حالة النوم، تعظيماً لحرمة المسجد وحفظاً لحصره عن تنجسها بالدم انتهى عبارة الجلال السيوطي رحمه الله تعالى. والمصرح به في كتبنا أنه لا يجوز إلقاء قشر القملة في المسجد، (وَ) يكره (تغطية أنفه، وفمه لما رويناه من أنه : « نَهَى عَنْ السَّدْل، وَأَنْ
And closing his eyes, and raising them to the sky, and stretching, and little action, and taking a louse and killing it... and [the text] 'al-Tabyin', and said in 'al-Bahr': placing the hand is established in Muslim and the sleeve is analogy. And in 'al-Khulasa': if he can take his lips with his teeth then he should do so, and place the back of his hand on his mouth, as in 'Mukhtarat al-Nawazil', and it should be with his right hand, and it is said: in standing and other than it with his left, likewise in 'al-Mujtaba'. (And) disliked is closing his eyes, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'When one of you stands in prayer, let him not close his eyes', [and because it contradicts] khushu', and it contains a type of frivolity, and leaving looking at the sunnah place, and because every limb and part has a share in this worship, so too the eye. And the dislike should be tanzihi if without necessity and no benefit; but if he fears losing khushu' due to seeing something that disturbs the mind, then closing them is not disliked, rather perhaps it is better, because then it is perfection of khushu' – said by the author of al-Bahr. (And) disliked is raising them to the sky, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'What is the matter with people who raise their eyes to the sky? They must desist or their eyesight will be snatched away' – as in al-Burhan. (And) stretching, because it is from laziness and it contradicts khushu'. (And) disliked is little action that contradicts prayer, and its individual instances are many, like plucking one hair or two hairs, and the difference between little and much action preceded. And Qadi Khan considered from it a single shot from a bow in the prayer of fear, and it is not performed except with two hands, and perhaps because in that situation it is not thought that he is not in prayer, since walking was permitted for him, so too the shot due to his need for it. (And) from it is taking a louse and killing it without excuse; for if a louse or flea distracts him or bites him, then taking is not disliked. And in 'Majma' al-Riwayat': it is disliked to take a louse and kill it, but he should bury it under pebbles. And in the saying of Abu Hanifa and narrated from him: if he takes a louse or buries it, he has done evil – end. And in 'al-Bazzaziyya': The Imam said: burying it is more beloved to me than killing it, and Muhammad said: killing it, and the second said: both are disliked – end. And covering his nose and mouth. And in 'al-Tajnis': from Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him: that killing a louse in prayer is more beloved to me than burying it, and all that is fine. Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, said: he does not kill the louse in prayer but buries it under pebbles, due to what was narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, that he was praying and took a louse and buried it, then recited the verse: 'Did We not make the earth a container?' [al-Mursalat 77:25]. And the justification for killing is that it removes harm from oneself, so there is no problem, like killing a snake or scorpion – end. And he said in al-Tajnis: also refraining from killing the louse is better – end. I said: and its justification is because it involves leaving action and avoiding the different opinion on impurity. Al-Jalal al-Suyuti said in 'al-Yanbu'': al-Zarkashi said: Malik, may Allah have mercy on him, disliked killing fleas and lice in the mosque, and al-Nawawi stated that if he kills them, he may not throw them in the mosque because they are carrion. And in the Musnad of Ahmad from Abu Ayyub said: 'A man found a louse in his garment, so he took it and threw it in the mosque, so the Messenger of Allah said to him: Do not do that; return it to your garment until you leave the mosque.' And Ibn al-Imad said: as for throwing lice in the mosque, if dead it is forbidden due to its impurity, and if alive, in the books of the Malikis it is forbidden to throw lice alive contrary to fleas, and the difference is that the flea lives by eating soil, unlike the louse; in throwing it there is torture by hunger, and that is not permissible, and he said: 'Indeed Allah has prescribed excellence in everything; so when you kill, kill well.' Based on this, it is forbidden to throw lice alive in the mosque and elsewhere, and it is forbidden for a man to throw his clothes while they have lice before killing them, and the better is not to kill it in the mosque, due to the hadith: 'When one of you finds a louse in his garment, let him wrap it and not throw it in the mosque' – narrated by Ahmad. And if he kills lice in his clothes and leaves them dead in them and prays in them, his prayer is not valid, because the carrion of lice and fleas are impure according to the correct view contrary to al-Qaffal, and a little of its blood in the garment is pardoned, even if he intentionally killed it, unlike skin because there is no difficulty in avoiding it. And if the blood of fleas appears on the mat of the mosque from someone sleeping in the mosque, concerning pardon for the one praying there is consideration, because avoidance is possible. And the sleeper should be ordered to place a barrier between himself and the mat while sleeping, to honor the sanctity of the mosque and protect its mat from being soiled by blood – end of the words of al-Jalal al-Suyuti. And it is explicitly stated in our books that it is not permissible to throw the shell of a louse in the mosque. (And) disliked is covering his nose and mouth, because we narrated that he forbade wrapping (sadl) and that...
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is a commentary (sharh) on Nur al-Idah, listing various disliked actions (makruhat) in prayer. The author first mentions the general list: closing eyes, raising eyes to the sky, stretching (tamattu), little actions, and taking/killing lice. He then expands on each ruling with proofs and scholarly discussion.

For closing the eyes: The hadith quoted is weak according to Hanafi scholars, but the dislike is based on it being contradicting khushu' and involving frivolity. The author clarifies that the dislike is tanzihi (not strictly prohibited) unless there is a necessity, such as fear of losing concentration due to distracting sights; then closing the eyes is not only permissible but preferable to preserve khushu'.

Raising eyes to the sky: A strong hadith (Bukhari) threatens loss of eyesight, so it is makruh. Stretching (tamattu) is from laziness and contrary to khushu'.

Little actions: Defined broadly, like plucking one or two hairs. The distinction between little and much action is discussed elsewhere. Qadi Khan included a single shot from a bow in the fear prayer because it is necessary and does not negate prayer.

Taking and killing lice is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute. Abu Hanifa prefers burying the louse, citing a hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, while Muhammad prefers killing it (removing harm, analogy to snake/scorpion). Abu Yusuf said both are disliked. The author notes that killing is cleaner, but burying avoids impurity differed upon. The passage then extends to rulings about lice in the mosque, quoting Malik and others, concluding that throwing dead or alive lice in the mosque is forbidden, and one should wrap it and remove it from the mosque.

The passage ends with covering nose and mouth, but the text is cut off. It mentions a hadith forbidding sadl (wrapping) and covering, likely referring to covering the face with a garment while praying, which is also makruh.

Key Terms
تغميض العينين (taghmīḍ al-ʿaynayn): Closing the eyes tightly during prayer
رفع البصر (rafʿ al-baṣar): Raising the gaze to the sky during prayer
تمطي (tamaṭṭī): Stretching the body lazily, yawning and extending limbs

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is closing the eyes in prayer not disliked?
A) When the imam is reciting loudly
B) When one fears losing khushu' due to distractions
C) When praying alone
D) When it is raining

Key Takeaway
Closing eyes in prayer is disliked unless needed to maintain concentration; raising eyes and stretching are disliked as they contradict khushu'.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Little Actions (al-ʿamal al-qalīl) in Prayer
Definition and ruling on little actions with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify examples of little actions (al-ʿamal al-qalīl) in prayer and distinguish them from much actions (al-ʿamal al-kathīr) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A little action that does not contradict the form of prayer is disliked; a much action invalidates it.

Not every movement during prayer is forbidden. The Hanafi school distinguishes between 'little action' (al-ʿamal al-qalīl) and 'much action' (al-ʿamal al-kathīr) based on custom and whether it disrupts the prayer's form. In this lesson, we explore what constitutes a little action, its ruling, and examples such as plucking a hair or shooting an arrow in the fear prayer.

Guided Path
1
Define 'little action' (al-ʿamal al-qalīl)
A minor action that does not significantly alter the state of prayer, e.g., plucking one or two hairs, flicking a louse, or making a small gesture.
The standard is what people customarily consider little.
2
Distinguish from 'much action' (al-ʿamal al-kathīr)
An action that disrupts the prayer's form (like both hands moving or three consecutive movements) invalidates the prayer. The boundary is based on customary judgment, not a fixed number.
This distinction is treated in detail elsewhere in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Identify the ruling on little actions
Little actions that do not contradict the prayer are makruh tanzihi. They are disliked but do not invalidate.
If the action is necessary (e.g., removing harm), the dislike disappears.
4
Analyze the example of a single arrow shot in fear prayer
Qadi Khan considered a single shot from a bow as little action because it is necessary and does not lead to the assumption that one is not praying, given that walking is already permitted in that situation.
This shows that necessity can override the general dislike.
5
Apply to new scenarios
Given a modern example (e.g., adjusting a phone on silent with one hand), decide whether it is qalil or kathir.
Use the customary standard and the test of whether it contradicts the form of prayer.

وتغميض عَيْنَيْهِ، ورَفْعُهُمَا للسّماء، والتَّمَطَّي، والعملُ القليلُ، وأَخذُ قَمْلَةٍ، وقَتْلُها .. و « التبيين»، وقال في « البحر ) : وضع اليد ثابت في مسلم والكم قياس، وفي «الخلاصة»: إن أمكنه أخذ شفتيه بسنه فليفعل، ويضع ظهر يده على فيه، كما في «مختارات النوازل»، ويكون بيمينه، وقيل: في القيام بها وفي غيره بيساره، كذا في المجتبى»، (وَ) يكره (تغميضُ عَيْنَيْهِ) لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( إذَا قَامَ أحَدُكُمْ في الصَّلاةِ فَلا يُغْمِضُ عَيْنَيْهِ ، [ ولأنه ينافي ] الخشوع، وفيه نوع عبث، وترك النظر إلى الموضع المسنون، ولأن كل عضو وطرف ذو حظ من هذه العبادة، فكذا العين، وينبغي أن تكون الكراهة تنزيهية إذا كان لغير ضرورة و [ لا ] مصلحة، أما لو خــاف فـوت الخشوع بسبب رؤية ما يفوق الخاطر فلا يكره غمضهما، بل ربما يكون أولى، لأنه حينئذ كمال للخشوع قاله صاحب البحر » . (و) يكره (رَفْعُهُما للسّماء) لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: « مَا بَالُ أقْوَامٍ يَرْفَعُونَ أَبْصَارَهُمْ إلى السَّمَاءِ لِيَنْتَهِين أو لتُخطفَنَّ أبصارهم ) كذا في ( البرهان»، (والتَّمَطي)) لأنه من التكاسل، وهو ينافي الخشوع. (و) يكره ( العملُ القليلُ) المنافي للصلاة، وأفراده كثيرة كنتف شعرة، أو شعرتين، وتقدم الفــرق بين العمل القليل والكثير، وجعل منه قاضي خان الرمية الواحدة عن القوس في صلاة الخوف ولا تقام إلا باليدين، ولعله لأن في تلك الحالة لا يظن به أنه ليس في الصلاة، لما أنـه لمـا أبـيـح لـه المشي، فكذا الرمية لاحتياجه إليها، (وَ) منه (أَخْذُ قَمْلَةٍ، وقَتْلُها ) من غير عذر، إذ لو شغلته أو شغله برغوث بالعض لا يكره الأخذ، وفي مجمع الروايات»: ويكره أن يأخذ قملة ويقتلها، لكن يدفنها تحت الحصى، وفي قول أبي حنيفة وروي عنه إن أخذ قملة أو دفنها فقد أساء انتهى. وفي « البزازية » : قال الإمام: دفنها فيها أحب من قتلها، وقال محمد قتلها، وقال الثاني: كلاهما مكروه انتهى.
وتغطية أنفه، وفمه. وفي « التجنيس : وعن محمد رحمه الله : أن قتل القملة في الصلاة أحب إلي من دفنها، وكـل ذلك لا بأس به، قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله : لا يقتل القملة في الصلاة ويدفنها تحت الحصى، لما روي عبد الله بن مسعود الله أنه كان يصلي فأخذ قملة ودفنها، ثم تلا قوله تعالى: ﴿أَلَمْ تَجَعَلِ الْأَرْضَ كفانا (١) [ المرسلات : ٢٥] ووجه القتل أن فيه إزالة الأذى عن نفسه، فلا يكون بـه بـأس، كقتل الحية والعقرب Based on this, it is forbidden to throw lice alive in the mosque and elsewhere, and it is forbidden for a man to throw his clothes while they have lice before killing them, and the better is not to kill it in the mosque, due to the hadith: 'When one of you finds a louse in his garment, let him wrap it and not throw it in the mosque' – narrated by Ahmad. And if he kills lice in his clothes and leaves them dead in them and prays in them, his prayer is not valid, because the carrion of lice and fleas are impure according to the correct view contrary to al-Qaffal, and a little of its blood in the garment is pardoned, even if he intentionally killed it, unlike skin because there is no difficulty in avoiding it. And if the blood of fleas appears on the mat of the mosque from someone sleeping in the mosque, concerning pardon for the one praying there is consideration, because avoidance is possible. And the sleeper should be ordered to place a barrier between himself and the mat while sleeping, to honor the sanctity of the mosque and protect its mat from being soiled by blood – end of the words of al-Jalal al-Suyuti. And it is explicitly stated in our books that it is not permissible to throw the shell of a louse in the mosque. (And) disliked is covering his nose and mouth, because we narrated that he forbade wrapping (sadl) and that...
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is a commentary (sharh) on Nur al-Idah, listing various disliked actions (makruhat) in prayer. The author first mentions the general list: closing eyes, raising eyes to the sky, stretching (tamattu), little actions, and taking/killing lice. He then expands on each ruling with proofs and scholarly discussion.

For closing the eyes: The hadith quoted is weak according to Hanafi scholars, but the dislike is based on it being contradicting khushu' and involving frivolity. The author clarifies that the dislike is tanzihi (not strictly prohibited) unless there is a necessity, such as fear of losing concentration due to distracting sights; then closing the eyes is not only permissible but preferable to preserve khushu'.

Raising eyes to the sky: A strong hadith (Bukhari) threatens loss of eyesight, so it is makruh. Stretching (tamattu) is from laziness and contrary to khushu'.

Little actions: Defined broadly, like plucking one or two hairs. The distinction between little and much action is discussed elsewhere. Qadi Khan included a single shot from a bow in the fear prayer because it is necessary and does not negate prayer.

Taking and killing lice is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute. Abu Hanifa prefers burying the louse, citing a hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, while Muhammad prefers killing it (removing harm, analogy to snake/scorpion). Abu Yusuf said both are disliked. The author notes that killing is cleaner, but burying avoids impurity differed upon. The passage then extends to rulings about lice in the mosque, quoting Malik and others, concluding that throwing dead or alive lice in the mosque is forbidden, and one should wrap it and remove it from the mosque.

The passage ends with covering nose and mouth, but the text is cut off. It mentions a hadith forbidding sadl (wrapping) and covering, likely referring to covering the face with a garment while praying, which is also makruh.

Key Terms
العمل القليل (al-ʿamal al-qalīl): A minor action in prayer that does not disrupt its form, e.g., plucking one hair.
العمل الكثير (al-ʿamal al-kathīr): A major action that contradicts the form of prayer, e.g., three consecutive movements or both hands doing something.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is considered a little action (al-ʿamal al-qalīl)?
A) Walking three steps forward
B) Plucking a single hair
C) Tying a turban with both hands
D) Wiping sweat from the forehead with a cloth

Key Takeaway
Little actions are disliked but do not invalidate prayer; necessity can make them permissible.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Lice in Prayer: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf and Disposal Rulings
Intra-Hanafi dispute and extended rulings on lice in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the different Hanafi positions on killing or burying lice during prayer and state the relied-upon view, as well as the rulings on disposing of lice in the mosque.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school prefers burying a louse under pebbles over killing it during prayer to avoid impurity and dispute.

Finding a louse on one's clothing during prayer is a practical scenario that classical scholars addressed in detail. Within the Hanafi school, there is a well-known intra-madhhab ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa preferred burying the louse, Muhammad allowed killing it, and Abu Yusuf disliked both. This lesson unpacks the arguments, the preferred view (mufta bihi), and the additional rulings on disposal in the mosque, including cross-madhhab perspectives.

Guided Path
1
State the intra-Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa: bury the louse under pebbles (no killing). Muhammad: killing is allowed (better than burying). Abu Yusuf: both actions are disliked.
The dispute is recorded in al-Bazzaziyya and other works.
2
Identify the proofs for each position
Abu Hanifa cites Ibn Mas'ud's practice: he buried a louse and recited the verse 'Did We not make the earth a container?' Muhammad uses qiyas with killing a snake/scorpion (removing harm). Abu Yusuf considers any action unnecessary.
The hadith of returning the louse to the garment until leaving the mosque supports avoiding killing in mosque.
3
Determine the mufta bihi (relied-upon view)
Later Hanafi fatwa prefers burying to avoid the impurity dispute and to stay away from killing unnecessarily. Killing is permitted if needed.
Imdad al-Fattah notes that refraining from killing is better.
4
Understand the rulings on disposal in the mosque
Throwing a dead louse in the mosque is forbidden because it is najis (carrion). Throwing a live louse is also forbidden to avoid torture. One should wrap it and remove it from the mosque.
This is agreed upon with other schools.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
If a person finds a louse during prayer, the best course is to gently remove it and bury it (if on earth) or wrap it and set aside. Killing is allowed if there is fear of being bitten or disturbed.
The modern context: carpets and indoor floors may require wrapping rather than burying.
