Dislike of Prayer in Work Clothes
Ruling and evidence for dislike of praying in everyday or work clothes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying in work clothes and identify the evidence from the Quran and the practice of 'Umar.

Core Idea
Prayer in work clothes is valid but disliked due to lack of adornment for standing before Allah.

This lesson addresses the ruling on praying in work clothes (thiyāb al-bidhla). The Hanafi school considers it disliked (makruh tanzih) because it shows disrespect to the dignity of standing before Allah. The evidence includes a Quranic verse encouraging adornment at mosques and an incident with 'Umar ibn al-Khattab who rebuked a man for such attire.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is performing salah while wearing work clothes (thiyāb al-bidhla). The ruling is dislike (makruh tanzih).
Dislike means the prayer is valid but better avoided.
2
Locate the first dalil (Quranic verse)
The verse 'Take your adornment at every mosque' (al-A'raf 7:31) is cited. Though exegetes primarily interpret it as covering the private parts, it also indicates general cleanliness and good appearance.
The verse is used here as an indirect proof for beautification.
3
Locate the second dalil (hadith of 'Umar)
It is reported that 'Umar saw a man praying in work clothes and rebuked him, saying, 'Allah is more deserving that you adorn yourself for Him.'
This shows the sahaba's understanding of proper attire for prayer.
4
Determine the nature of the dislike
The dislike is based on the lack of adornment and respect, not on impurity. The prayer remains valid.
This is a tanzihi (light) dislike, not tahrimi (prohibition).
5
Note cross-madhhab status
The ruling is mukhtalaf fih; some schools may not consider this dislike as strong, but all agree on the desirability of clean attire.
The Hanafi position is supported by transmitted evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) تكره (الصَّلاةُ في ثيابِ البِدْلَةِ) بكسـر الـبـاء وسـكـون الـذال المعجمة: ثوب لايصان ولا يحفظ عن الدنس ونحوه، وابتذال الثوب وغيره امتهانه، وقيل: ما يلبس في البيت ولا يذهب به إلى الكبراء، وكذا ثياب المهنة كحكمة في أوزانها وبفتح الميم والـهـاء مـعـاً وهي: الخدمة والعمل، فيتحرز عنها، تكميلاً لرعاية مقام الوقوف بين يدي الله سبحانه وتعالـى بـمـا أمكن، من تجميل الظاهر والباطن، وفي قوله تعالى: ﴿خُذُوا زِينَتَكُمْ عِندَ كُلِّ مَسْجِدٍ [الأعراف : ٣١] إشارة إليه، وإن كان المراد به ستر العورة على ما ذكره أهل التفسير، كما تقدم وقال في « التجنيس» : تكــره في ثياب البذلة؛ لما روي « أنَّ عمر الله رأى رجلاً فعل ذلك فقال: أرأيت لو كنتُ أرسلتك إلى بعض النَّاس، أكنْتَ تَمرُّ في ثيابِكَ هَذِهِ؟ فقال: لا، فقال عمر لا له: الله أحَقُّ أَنْ تَتَزَيَّن لَهُ» (۱) انتهى.
And it is disliked to pray in clothes of bidhla (work clothes) — with kasra on the ba and sukun on the dhal: a garment that is not protected or preserved from dirt and the like, and wasting the garment etc. means treating it disrespectfully. It is said: what is worn at home and not taken to important people. Similarly, clothes of labor (mihnah), which is service and work. So one should avoid them, to complete the observance of standing before Allah Almighty as much as possible, by beautifying the outward and inward. And in the verse 'Take your adornment at every mosque' (al-A'raf 31) there is an indication to this, even if the intent is covering the private parts according to the exegetes, as has preceded. And it is said in al-Tajnīs: it is disliked to pray in work clothes due to what is related that 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) saw a man doing that and said: 'Do you think that if I sent you to some people, would you go in these clothes?' He said: No. So 'Umar said: Allah is more deserving that you adorn yourself for Him.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on praying in work clothes (thiyāb al-bidhla). These are garments that are not kept clean or are used for daily labor, implying they may be dirty or shabby. The dislike is due to the lack of respect and adornment appropriate for standing before Allah. The proof includes Quranic verse 7:31 ('Take your adornment at every mosque'), which is interpreted to encourage cleanliness and good appearance, and a famous incident with 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, who rebuked a man for praying in such clothes, saying that Allah deserves more adornment than any human. The text also mentions that this is about avoiding disrespect, not about the clothes being impure per se. The Hanafi school emphasizes the etiquette of prayer, including wearing one's best clothes.

Key Terms
ثياب البذلة (thiyāb al-bidhla): Garments that are not kept clean or are worn for work; clothes considered disrespectable for important occasions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) They lack adornment and respect due to Allah
C) They are uncomfortable
D) They are against the Sunnah

Key Takeaway
Prayer in work clothes is valid but disliked (makruh tanzih) because it fails to show proper adornment and reverence for standing before Allah.

Praying with Uncovered Head: Intention Determines the Ruling
Ruling with proof on intention-based distinction for uncovered head in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying with an uncovered head and explain how intention (laziness vs. humility) changes the ruling.

Core Idea
Intention transforms makrūh into mustaḥabb: laziness vs. humility in uncovering the head.

This passage from Imdād al-Fattāḥ clarifies a common point of confusion: is it always disliked to pray with an uncovered head? The Hanafi school distinguishes based on intention. Uncovering out of laziness abandons dignity (waqār), but uncovering out of humility and supplication (tadhallul wa tadarru‘) is recommended because prayer is built upon khushu‘. The text also touches on the nature of khushu‘ itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is praying with the head uncovered. The default is makrūh tanzīhī (disliked) when done without a valid reason.
2
Determine the cause (illah) of dislike
The dislike stems from abandoning dignity (waqār) when one is able to cover but does so out of laziness or considering it burdensome.
3
Recognize the exception based on intention
If the intention is humility and supplication (tadhallul wa tadarru‘), the ruling changes to recommended (mustaḥabb).
4
Understand the proof (dalīl)
The proof is that prayer is built on khushu‘; uncovering for humility aligns with khushu‘. The text cites al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd and al-Munyah.
5
Explore the intra-Hanafi nuance
Note the slight difference between 'lā ba's' (no harm) and explicit recommendation. The muftā bihī is recommendation when done out of humility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) تكره الصلاة وهو (مكشوف الرأس) قادراً على سترها وفعله تكاسلاً واستثقالاً لتغطيتها لا استخفافاً، لأنــه كفر والعياذ بالله تعالى، فكشفها للكسل ونحوه مكروه؛ لما فيه من ترك الوقار، إذ (لا) يكره (للتذلل والتَّضَرُّعِ الله تعالى، ويستحب له ذلك، لأن مبنى الصلاة على الخشوع، كذا في « التجنيس والمزيــد » وقال في ( المنية » : لا بأس إذا فعله تذللاً، قال شارحها وفي قوله لا بأس إشارة إلى أن الأولى أن لا يفعله، وأن يتذلل ويخشع بقلبه، فإنهما من أفعال القلب انتهى. ولكن قد علمت نص استحباب ذلك. تنبيه: قد جزم شارح المنية ) بأن الخشوع من أعمال القلب، كما علمت، وقد قال الجلال السيوطي في ( الينبوع » : اختلفوا في الخشوع هل هو من أعمال القلب كالخوف، أو من أعمال الجوارح كالسكون، أو هو عبارة عن المجموع ؟؟؟ وقال الرازي: الثالث أولى، وفي «شرح المهذب » : روى البيهقي عن علي قال : « الخُشُوعُ فِي القَلْب ) ، وعن جماعة من السلف الخشوع في الصلاة: السكون فيها ، وقال البغوي في ث شرح السنة » : : الخشوع قريب من الخضوع، إلا أن الخضوع في البدن والخشوع في البدن والبصر والصوت انتهى.
And it is disliked to pray while having the head uncovered, if one is able to cover it and does so out of laziness and considering covering burdensome, not out of disrespect, for that would be disbelief. So uncovering out of laziness etc. is disliked because it abandons dignity. It is not disliked if done for humility and supplication to Allah; rather it is recommended, because prayer is built upon khushu'. This is as stated in al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd. And it is said in al-Munyah: There is no harm if he does it out of humility. Its commentator said: The phrase 'no harm' indicates that it is better not to do it, and that he should humble himself and have khushu' in his heart, for they are actions of the heart. But you have learned the text of its recommendation. Note: The commentator of al-Munyah decisively stated that khushu' is an action of the heart, as you have learned. Jalāl al-Suyūṭī said in al-Yanbū': They differed about khushu': is it an action of the heart like fear, or an action of the limbs like stillness, or is it a combination? Al-Rāzī said the third is better. In Sharḥ al-Muhadhdhab, al-Bayhaqī narrated from 'Alī: 'Khushu' is in the heart.' And from a group of salaf: Khushu' in prayer is stillness. Al-Baghawī said in Sharḥ al-Sunnah: Khushu' is close to khushu', except that khushu' is in the body, and khushu' is in the body, sight, and voice.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage covers two related matters: the ruling on praying with an uncovered head, and a discussion on the nature of khushu'. For the first, the ruling depends on intention. If one uncovers the head out of laziness or considering covering a burden, it is disliked because it abandons the dignity (waqār) expected in prayer. If done out of humility and supplication to Allah, it is recommended (mustaḥabb), because prayer is based on khushu'. The text cites al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd and al-Munyah. There is a slight nuance: Ibn 'Ābidīn (commentator of al-Munyah) suggests the preferred view is not to do it, but the text confirms the recommendation. The second part is a tangent on khushu', quoting Suyūṭī, Rāzī, and others, discussing whether khushu' is a physical state or internal. This is relevant because the ruling on uncovering the head is tied to the concept of khushu' and humility.

Key Terms
مكشوف الرأس (makshūf al-ra's): Having the head uncovered during prayer.
الخشوع (al-khushū'): Humility, focus, and presence of heart in prayer.

Key Takeaway
Intention (niyyah) is the decisive factor that shifts the ruling from makrūh to mustaḥabb in the Hanafi view on uncovering the head during prayer.

Prayer in the Presence of Desired Food
Ruling on praying when food one desires is present

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying in the presence of desired food, cite the hadith proof, and explain why the ruling is makruh tanzih.

Core Idea
Prayer when desired food is present is valid but deficient — eat first for full reward.

The Hanafi school teaches that prayer is disliked when one's desired food is present, especially due to hunger. This is not a prohibition of validity but a call to protect khushu' (focus). The proof is a well-known hadith that many may misunderstand as nullifying the prayer. In this lesson, we unpack the ruling, its evidence, and the correct interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying (any prayer, obligatory or supererogatory) when food that one desires is present and one is inclined to eat due to hunger. The ruling is 'makruh tanzih' (disliked but not prohibited).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'Lā ṣalāta bi-ḥaḍrati al-ṭa’āmi wa lā huwa yudāfi‘uhu al-akhbatān' (There is no [complete] prayer when food is present, nor when one is suppressing the two filths). This hadith is narrated by Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'lā ṣalāta' is interpreted as negation of perfection, not validity. The presence of desired food distracts the heart, diminishing khushu'. Thus, the prayer is valid but flawed in reward.
Hanafi usul: 'al-nafy' in such contexts is interpreted as denial of completeness when evidence supports that.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
There is no intra-Hanafi or inter-madhhab dispute on the ruling itself— all schools agree prayer is disliked in this state. The practical difference is whether one should postpone prayer to eat or not. The Hanafi position is to eat first if one is hungry and the food is present, unless the prayer time is about to expire.
5
Understand the mufta bihi and modern application
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that it is disliked (makruh tanzih). If one prays while hungry and food is before him, the prayer is valid but deficient in khushu’. It is better to eat first, provided there is enough time for prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) تكره (بحضرة طعــام يـمـيـلُ) طبعـه ( إلـيـه)، باشتهائه في تلك الحالة لجوع به؛ لقوله : « لا صَلاةَ بِحَضْرَةِ الطَّعَامِ وَلَا هُوَ يُدَافِعُهُ الأَخْبَتَانِ»
And it is disliked to pray in the presence of food to which one's nature inclines, due to his craving in that state from hunger; because of his saying (ﷺ): 'There is no prayer when food is present, nor when one is suppressing the two filths.'
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This is a concise ruling that prayer is disliked when food is present and one desires to eat it due to hunger. The proof is a hadith: 'Lā ṣalāta bi-ḥaḍrati al-ṭa'āmi wa lā huwa yudāfi'uhu al-akhbatān' (There is no [complete] prayer when food is present, nor when one is suppressing the two filths). The hadith is reported by Muslim and Abu Dawud. The word 'lā ṣalāta' here is interpreted as denial of completeness, not validity, so the prayer is valid but deficient in khushu'. The ruling is similar to the earlier one about suppressing urine: distraction from food prevents focus and khushu'. The Hanafi school applies this to any food that one desires, not necessarily only when hungry, but the text specifies being inclined due to hunger.

Key Terms
بحضرة طعام (bi-ḥaḍrati ṭa'ām): When food is present and one desires it, especially due to hunger.

Key Takeaway

Prayer with Uncovered Head: Intention Determines the Ruling
Distinguishes ruling by intention, with additional discussion on khushu'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the disliked and recommended cases of praying with uncovered head in the Hanafi school and apply the ruling based on the worshipper's intention.

Core Idea
Praying with uncovered head: makruh when lazy, recommended when humble—intention governs.

Covering the head is generally recommended in prayer, but what if a person prays with his head uncovered? The Hanafi school teaches that the ruling depends entirely on the intention. If done out of laziness, it is disliked; if done out of humility and a desire to enhance khushu', it is not only permissible but recommended. The source passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies this distinction and delves into the meaning of khushu' itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general category
The act is praying with an uncovered head (maksuf al-ra's). The base ruling from the matn is that it is makruh. But the sharh expands by examining the worshipper's state of mind.
2
Distinguish the two intentions
The author distinguishes: (1) doing it out of laziness or feeling burdensome to cover (takasul, istithqal) — this is makruh tanzih. (2) doing it out of humility and supplication (tadhallul, tadarru') — this is mustahabb.
Laziness vs. humility: the key differentiator.
3
State the ruling for each case
Laziness → makruh (disliked). Humility → mustahabb (recommended). The proof: prayer is built on khushu', and uncovering for humility aids that purpose.
The matn's general karahah is qualified by the intention.
4
Understand the dalil: khushu' as the basis
The sharh quotes 'prayer is based on khushu''. If uncovering increases khushu', it is recommended. If it reduces dignity (waqar), it is disliked. This is a talil (rationale) linking the ruling to the purpose of prayer.
Khushu' is both heart and body in Hanafi view.
5
Note the intra-madhhab discussion on khushu'
The tanbih (note) discusses whether khushu' is purely a heart action or includes bodily stillness. The Hanafi view leans toward both, but the recommendation of uncovering for humility assumes khushu' includes body actions.
This refines the dalil: the ruling depends on which definition of khushu' one adopts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And with uncovered head not for humility and supplication, and in the presence of food one desires. Congregation after starting alone, and demolishing a mosque to build better than it was, thus in al-Burhan end. The implication of his saying: 'not permissible' necessitates certainty, and prayer is disliked while he is with uncovered head when able to cover it, and he does so out of laziness and feeling burdensome to cover it, not out of contempt, because that is kufr (may Allah protect). So uncovering it for laziness and the like is disliked, because it involves leaving dignity. It is not disliked when done for humility and supplication to Allah Almighty, and it is recommended for him to do so, because prayer is based on khushu'. Thus in al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd. And it is said in al-Munya: There is no harm if he does it out of humility. Its commentator said: In his saying 'no harm' is an indication that the preferable is not to do it, and that he should humble himself and be humble in his heart, for these are actions of the heart. End. But you have learned the text of its recommendation. Note: The commentator of al-Munya affirmed that khushu' is an action of the heart, as you learned. Al-Suyuti in al-Yanbu' said: They differed about khushu': is it an action of the heart like fear, or of the limbs like stillness, or is it an expression of the combination? Al-Razi said the third is better. In Sharh al-Muhadhdhab: al-Bayhaqi reported from Ali: 'Khushu' is in the heart.' And from a group of salaf: khushu' in prayer is stillness in it. Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on praying with an uncovered head. The author distinguishes between two cases: if one uncovers out of laziness or feeling it burdensome to cover, it is makruh because it abandons proper dignity in prayer. However, if one uncovers as an act of humility and supplication to Allah, it is not only permissible but recommended (mustahabb) because the foundation of prayer is khushu' (humility). The author cites al-Munya which says 'no harm' but indicates the first preference is to cover. A lengthy note (tanbih) discusses the nature of khushu', quoting various scholars: some hold it is purely a heart action, others include bodily stillness, and a third view combines both. The Hanafi position is that khushu' involves both heart and body, but the core is in the heart.

Key Terms
الخشوع (al-khushu'): Humility and stillness in prayer, involving both heart and body.
مكشوف الرأس (maksuf al-ra's): Uncovered head, i.e., without a cap or turban in prayer.
تكاسل (takasul): Laziness, showing reluctance to cover the head.
تذلل (tadhallul): Humility, lowliness before Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Makruh, because covering is always better.
B) Mustahabb, because it enhances khushu'.
C) Haram, because it violates the sunnah.
D) Mubah, neutral.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the ruling on praying with an uncovered head depends entirely on the intention: laziness makes it disliked, humility makes it recommended.

Prayer in Presence of Desired Food: Ruling and Evidence
Explains dislike of praying when food is present and one desires it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules prayer as makruh tanzih when desired food is present and apply the hadith evidence correctly.

Core Idea
Prayer with food present is valid but disliked; preserve khushu by eating first.

This passage addresses a common situation: you are hungry, the food is served, and the prayer time enters. Should you pray first or eat first? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on authentic hadith, prioritizing the concentration of the heart (khushu) in prayer. Let us examine the evidence and the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing prayer when one's desired food is present and one is hungry. The ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked, not sinful but better to avoid).
The ruling applies only when the food is desired and one is genuinely hungry.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith: 'La salata bi hadrat al-ta'am' (No prayer in presence of food). This is found in Muslim and Abu Dawud.
The negation 'la salata' does not mean the prayer is invalid; it indicates incompleteness or dislike in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase shows that the prayer is deficient due to lack of khushu. The Hanafi principle: negation of 'prayer' in this context means it is not perfect, not that it is void.
This interpretation is supported by other hadith that command eating first.
4
Resolve conflicting evidence
Another hadith says: 'Do not delay prayer for food.' The author clarifies that this refers to delaying prayer beyond its time, not delaying to eat first. The hadith commanding to begin with supper takes precedence.
The resolution is based on clear instruction from the two Sahihs (Bukhari and Muslim).
5
Determine the practical implication
If food is ready and prayer time has entered, eat first if you are hungry and the food is desired. If eating would cause missing the prayer time, then pray first to avoid sin.
The overriding principle is to avoid distraction and preserve khushu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it is disliked to pray in the presence of food that one's nature inclines to, due to craving in that state because of hunger; because of his saying: 'There is no prayer in the presence of food nor when the two foul things are pressing.' And whatever distracts the mind and impairs khushu', and counting verses, and counting tasbih with the hand. Muslim narrated it. And what is in Abu Dawud: 'Do not delay prayer for food or anything else' is interpreted as delaying it beyond its time, because of the clear hadith: 'When the supper of any of you is placed and the prayer is called, begin with supper and do not rush until you finish it.' Narrated by the two shaykhs. Another wording: 'When the supper is presented, begin with it before you pray the maghrib prayer and do not rush from your supper.' He ordered it to be presented so that khushu' does not go away due to preoccupation of thought, thus in al-Burhan.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage explains that praying when one's desired food is present and one is hungry is makruh. The proof is a hadith: 'There is no prayer in the presence of food nor when the two foul things (urine and stool) are pressing.' This indicates that one should eat first to allow full concentration. The author clarifies that another hadith prohibiting delaying prayer for food is interpreted as delaying beyond the prayer time, not delaying to eat first. The preferred action is to eat if the food is ready and prayer time has entered, to avoid distraction. This ruling is based on preserving khushu' in prayer.

Key Terms
الخشوع (khushu'): Humility and concentration in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should one do if food is served at the time of maghrib prayer?
A) Pray first, then eat
B) Eat first, then pray
C) Delay both until after the time
D) It does not matter

Key Takeaway
Prayer in the presence of desired food is makruh tanzih; one should eat first to preserve khushu.

Counting Tasbih with the Hand in Prayer: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on counting in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on counting tasbih with the hand in obligatory prayer and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Counting tasbih with the hand in obligatory prayer is disliked (makruh) according to Abu Hanifa but permissible according to the two companions.

Prayer requires khushu' (focus and humility). The Hanafi school discusses whether counting verses or tasbih with the hand during prayer distracts from this focus. In this passage, the author presents the ruling of Abu Hanifa and the differing view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, shedding light on how the principle of avoiding anything that impairs khushu' is applied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general context
The act is counting verses (ayat) or tasbih (glorifications) with the hand during prayer, e.g., by closing fingers or using a rosary.
The passage also mentions counting with the heart and tongue, but the dispute focuses on hand.
2
State the primary Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Abu Hanifa rules it as makruh tanzih (disliked) because it reduces khushu'.
The prayer remains valid, but it is discouraged.
3
State the opposing position (Sahibayn)
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani consider it permissible (la ba'sa) as there is no explicit prohibition.
Some reports indicate Muhammad may have agreed with Abu Hanifa.
4
Note the reported variations
The passage mentions disagreements on whether the dislike applies to obligatory or supererogatory prayers, and whether counting outside prayer is disliked.
The majority hold that counting tasbih outside prayer is not disliked.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position for fatwa is the dislike in obligatory prayer as per Abu Hanifa, preserving khushu'.
This is recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) تكره بحضرة كل ما يَشْغَلُ البال)، كزينة، (وَ) بحضرة ما (يُخِلُّ بالخشوع) كلهو ولعب؛ لمـا ذكرنا، ولذا « نَهَى النَّبِيُّ عليه الصلاة والسلام عَنِ الإِتْيَانِ  ِللصَّلاةِ سَعْياً بِالهَرْوَلَةِ ، ولم يكن ذلك مراداً في الأمر بالسعي للجمعة، بل الذهاب بالسكينة والوقار، (وَ) لذا يكره في الصلاة (عــد الآي)) جمع آية، وهي: الجملة المقدرة من القرآن، وتطلق بمعنى العلامة، وبمعنى القصد والرسالة، وكذا عد السور، (وَ) عد ( التَّسْبِيحُ)، وقوله (باليد ) قيد لكراهة عد الآي والتسبيح، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى، خلافاً لهما، وذلك بأن يكون بقبض الأصابع، أو بسبحة يمسكها بيده، ولا يكره الغمز بالأنامل في موضعها، ولا الإحصاء بالقلب اتفاقاً، والعد باللسان مفسد اتفاقاً كذا في شرح الديري » ، ولكن قال في مجمع الروايات : قيل: أراد الشـيـخ بـه الـعــد بالأصابع، وقيل: بالقلب والأصابع أيضاً؛ لأنه ينقص من الخشوع وقالا : لا بأس به، وقيل: محمـد مـع أبـي حنيفة، وقيل: لا بأس في التطوع إجماعاً، وإنما الخلاف في المكتوبة، وقيل: يـكــره في المكتوبة إجماعاً، وإنما الخلاف في التطوع، واختلف في عد التسبيح خارج الصلاة، وقال في «شـــرح الديري»: ذهب الأكثر أنه لا يكره، وقال في المستصفى»: وهو الصحيح. تنبيه: يناسب المقام ذكر صلاة التسبيح، وصورتها ما روى صاحب السنن بإسناده إلى عكرمة،
And it is disliked in the presence of anything that distracts the mind, like adornment; and in the presence of anything that impairs khushu', like play and amusement, because of what we mentioned. Therefore the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) forbade coming to prayer running and hurrying, and that was not intended in the command to hasten to Friday, but rather to go with tranquility and dignity. Hence it is disliked in prayer to count verses (ayat) - plural of ayah: a defined sentence of the Quran, also used for sign, purpose, message; similarly counting surahs; and counting tasbih; and his saying 'with the hand' is a restriction for the dislike of counting verses and tasbih. This is according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) contrary to the two companions. That is by closing the fingers or by a subha (rosary) held in the hand. Pressing with fingertips in their places and counting with the heart are not disliked by agreement. Counting with the tongue invalidates the prayer by agreement, thus in Sharh al-Dayri. But it is said in Majma' al-Riwayat: Some said the shaykh meant counting with the fingers; some said with the heart and also the fingers because it reduces khushu'. The two companions said: there is no harm. Some said Muhammad is with Abu Hanifa. Some said there is no harm in supererogatory prayer by consensus, and the difference is in obligatory prayer. Some said it is disliked in obligatory prayer by consensus, and the difference is in supererogatory. There is difference about counting tasbih outside the prayer. It is said in Sharh al-Dayri: the majority hold it is not disliked, and in al-Mustasfa: that is the correct view. Note: It is appropriate here to mention the prayer of tasbih; its form is as narrated by the author of al-Sunan with his chain to 'Ikrimah...
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage covers the dislike of anything that distracts the mind (like adornment, play) and specifically focuses on counting verses or tasbih with the hand during prayer. The author explains that counting with fingers or a rosary is makruh according to Abu Hanifa because it reduces khushu', but the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it permissible. Various opinions are reported: some say Muhammad agreed with Abu Hanifa; some say the difference only applies to obligatory prayers, while in supererogatory it is agreed upon. Counting with the heart is not disliked, and counting with the tongue invalidates prayer. Outside prayer, counting tasbih is not disliked according to the majority. The passage ends with a note about Salat al-Tasbih (but the text cuts off).

Key Terms
عد الآي (add al-ay): Counting the verses of the Quran during prayer, usually with the fingers.
التسبيح باليد (al-tasbih bi al-yad): Counting glorifications of Allah with the hand, e.g., using fingers or a rosary.
الخشوع (al-khushu'): Focus, humility, and presence of heart in prayer.
مكروه تنزيهي (makruh tanzihi): A disliked action that is not sinful; avoiding it is meritorious but not required.

Counting tasbih with the hand in obligatory prayer is disliked (makruh tanzih) according to the mufta bihi of the Hanafi school, but the prayer remains valid.

Ruling on Counting Verses and Tasbih During Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on counting with the hand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on counting verses/tasbih with the hand during prayer and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two companions.

Core Idea
Counting with the hand in obligatory prayer is disliked according to Abu Hanifa, but permissible when needed per the Sahibayn.

You are in prayer and lose count of rak'ahs or tasbih. You instinctively start counting with your fingers. Is this allowed? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions disagree. This lesson extracts the ruling from Imdad al-Fattah and maps the internal Hanafi positions, clarifying when counting is disliked, permissible, or even invalid.

Guided Path
1
State the act and the ruling
What is the specific action (counting with the hand during prayer) and what is the ruling according to Abu Hanifa?
The passage specifies 'with the hand' as a key condition.
2
Identify the opposing view
The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold it is permissible (ja'iz) and not disliked.
Some narrations place Muhammad with Abu Hanifa.
3
Analyze the basis of each position
Abu Hanifa bases his view on preserving khushu' (wajib). The Sahibayn see no explicit prohibition and permit it as an aid.
The text mentions that counting with the tongue invalidates prayer by consensus.
4
Note the nuances and exceptions
Counting by pressing fingertips or mentally is never disliked. Counting outside prayer is also not disliked.
The compelled person (muqtadir) may act according to the Sahibayn.
5
Determine the tarjih (relied-upon position)
The mufta bihi is that counting with the hand is disliked in obligatory prayer, but the needy person may follow the Sahibayn.
Cited from Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir.

أَمْنَحُكَ عَشْرَ خِصَالٍ، زاد صاحب « البحر » : « ألا أعطيك، ألا أفْعَلُ بِكَ عَشْرَ خِصَالٍ، إِذَا أَنْتَ فَعَلْتَ ذَلِكَ غَفَرَ اللهُ لَكَ ذَنْبِكَ أوَّله وَ آخِرِهِ، قديمَهُ وحديثَهُ، خطأه وعمده، صغيره وكبيره، سره وعلانيته: أن تصلي أربـع رکعات تقرأ في كل ركعة فاتحةَ الكِتَابِ وسورة، فإذا فرغت من القِرَاءَةِ فِي أَوَّلِ رَكْعَةٍ وَأَنْتَ قَائِمٌ قلت: سبحانَ اللهِ، والحمدُ لله، ولا إلَهَ إِلَّا عشراً، ثمَّ تَرْفَعُ رَأْسَكَ [ من السجود ] فتقولُها عشراً، ثم تسجدُ فتقولُهَا عَشْرَاً، ثم ترفع رأسَكَ فتقولُهَا عشراً، فذلك خمس وسبعونَ في كُلِّ رَكْعَةٍ، تفعلُ ذلِكَ في أربعِ رَكْعَاتٍ، إِنِ كُلِّ سَنةٍ مَرَّةً، فَإِنْ لَمْ تَفْعَلْ فَفِي عُمُرِكَ مَرَّةً » انتهى. وقال « صاحب البحر » : رواه أبــو داود، وابن ماجه، والطبراني، وقال في آخره: « وَلَوْ كَانَتْ ذُنُوبُكَ مِثْلَ زَبَدِ البَحْرِ وَرَمْلِ عَالِجٍ، غَفَرَ اللَّهِ لك» . قال الحافظ عبد العظيم المنذري : وقد روي هذا الحديث من طرق كثيرة عن جماعة من الصحابة، وأمثلها حديث عكرمة هذا وقد صححه جماعة انتهى. وذكر فخـر الإسلام في «شرح الجامع الصغير قال أصحابنا : إن احتاج المرء إلى العد يعد إشارة لا إفصاحاً، ويعمل بقولهما المضطر انتهى.
Thus, it is disliked in prayer to count verses (ayah) – plural of ayah, which is a defined sentence from the Quran, and it is also used to mean sign, intention, and message – and likewise counting surahs, and counting tasbih. His saying 'with the hand' is a qualification for the dislike of counting verses and tasbih. This is according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). This is by clenching the fingers or using a rosary held in the hand. Pressing with the fingertips in their places is not disliked, nor is counting with the heart by agreement. Counting with the tongue invalidates (the prayer) by agreement, as in Sharh al-Dayri. But it is said in Majma' al-Riwayat: Some said al-Shaykh intended counting with the fingers, and some said with the heart and fingers as well because it diminishes khushu'. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: There is no harm in it. And it is said: Muhammad is with Abu Hanifa. And it is said: There is no harm in supererogatory (nafl) prayer by consensus, and the difference is only in obligatory prayer. And it is said: It is disliked in obligatory prayer by consensus, and the difference is only in supererogatory prayer. And there is difference regarding counting tasbih outside prayer. It is said in Sharh al-Dayri: The majority held that it is not disliked, and in al-Mustasfa it is said: That is the correct position. A beneficial note: It is appropriate at this juncture to mention Salat al-Tasbih, and its form is what the author of the Sunan narrated with his chain to 'Ikrimah, from Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to al-'Abbas ibn 'Abd al-Muttalib: 'O my uncle, shall I grant you ten characteristics...' (the long hadith follows). The author of al-Bahr added: 'Shall I give you? Shall I do with you ten characteristics? If you do that, Allah will forgive your sins, first and last, old and new, mistake and intentional, minor and major, secret and open: that you pray four rak'ahs...' (hadith continues). And the author of al-Bahr said: Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, and al-Tabarani narrated it, and at the end: 'Even if your sins are like the foam of the sea and the sand of 'Alij, Allah would forgive you.' Al-Hafiz 'Abd al-'Azim al-Mundhiri said: This hadith has been narrated through many chains from a group of Companions, and the best of them is this hadith of 'Ikrimah, and a group declared it authentic. Fakhr al-Islam in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir said: Our companions said: If a person needs to count, he should count by gesture, not by speaking out; and one who is compelled acts according to their (the two companions') statement. End.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling on counting verses and tasbih during prayer. The author begins by stating that counting Qur'anic verses, surahs, and tasbih is disliked (makruh) in prayer, and specifies that this dislike applies when done with the hand (by clenching fingers or using a rosary). This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. However, his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, differ: according to them, it is permissible and not disliked. The text then explains that counting by pressing fingertips is not disliked, nor is counting mentally (by heart) according to all. Counting with the tongue invalidates the prayer by consensus. The passage further reports variant opinions: some narrate that Muhammad actually agreed with Abu Hanifa; some say the dislike is only for obligatory prayers, not supererogatory; others say the opposite. There is also discussion about counting tasbih outside of prayer, where the majority and the correct view according to al-Mustasfa hold it is not disliked. The author then adds a beneficial note (tanbih) mentioning the prayer of tasbih (Salat al-Tasbih) and narrates its form via a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas. The hadith describes a specific prayer with 75 tasbihs per rak'ah, and the great reward for it. Finally, the passage cites Fakhr al-Islam stating that if one needs to count, it should be by gesture only, and the compelled person acts according to the two companions' ruling.

Key Terms
الآي (al-āy): Plural of āyah; a verse from the Qur'an, defined as a complete sentence from the Qur'an.
التسبيح (al-tasbīḥ): Saying 'Subhanallah' or the general act of glorifying Allah; here specifically counting it with the hand during prayer.
الخشوع (al-khushūʿ): Humility and concentration in prayer; it is considered wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school. Disruption of khushu' makes an action disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on counting tasbih with the hand during an obligatory prayer?
A) It is permissible without any dislike.
B) It is disliked (makruh) because it diminishes khushu'.
C) It invalidates the prayer.
D) It is recommended (sunnah) to increase concentration.

Key Takeaway
Counting with the hand during obligatory prayer is disliked by Abu Hanifa, but permissible when needed per the Sahibayn; counting with fingertips or heart is never disliked.

The Ruling on the Imam Standing in the Mihrab: Cause and Dispute
Explains the ruling and differing opinions on imam standing inside the mihrab during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam standing in the mihrab and explain the two different causes (illa) reported in the madhhab.

Core Idea
The imam standing in the mihrab is disliked; the dispute is whether the cause is resemblance to the People of the Book or obscuring the imam's actions from the congregation.

This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah addresses a practical issue in congregational prayer: where should the imam stand? Specifically, it rules on the imam standing inside the mihrab, the niche in the qibla wall. While the ruling is clear – it is disliked (makruh) – the cause behind the dislike is debated among Hanafi scholars. Understanding this ikhtilaf on the 'illa helps us apply the ruling correctly in different mihrab designs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal ruling
What is the hukm for the imam standing in the mihrab? Find the explicit statement in the passage.
The ruling is makruh tanzihi (disliked, not prohibited or invalidating).
2
Distinguish included and excluded actions
Note what is disliked and what is not: only standing completely inside is disliked; standing outside or prostrating inside is not.
This helps avoid over-generalization.
3
Analyze the first cause: tashabbuh bi-ahl al-kitab
Why does resemblance to the People of the Book lead to karahah? The majority view is that it is disliked because it imitates their practice of placing the imam in a special spot.
Tashabbuh is a well-established basis for karahah in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Analyze the second cause: ishtibah al-hal
How does obscuring the imam's condition from the congregation contravene the purpose of his forward position? The imam is placed in front so that his actions are visible; if the mihrab hides him, it defeats the purpose.
This view is attributed to Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani and others.
5
Apply the ikhtilaf to a latticed mihrab
If the mihrab is latticed so that the imam is visible, consider each cause: tashabbuh remains, so dislike persists; ishtibah is removed, so some say no dislike.
The passage presents both opinions without definitively choosing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يكره قيام الإمام) بجملته ( في المحراب)، لا قيامه خارجه وسجوده فيه، سمي محراباً؛ لأن المصلي يحارب الشيطان والنفس بالقيام إليه، وقد اختلفوا في عـلـة الـكـراهـة، فذهب الأكثر إلى أنها للتشبه بأهل الكتاب؛ لأنهم يخصون إمامهم بمكان وحده، والتشبه بـهم مكروه، وذهب جماعة - منهم الفقيه ( أبو جعفر الهندواني » - إلى أنها لاشتباه الحـال عـلـى مـن عـن يمينـه ويساره، والتقدم شرع للتيسير على القوم ليظهر حاله لهم، فإذا أفضى إلى خلاف موضوعه كره، فلـــو كان الطاق مشبكاً بحيث لا يخفى حال القيام فيه قيل: لا يكره لانتفاء العـلـة، وهي اشتباه الحال، وقيل: يكره لوجود العلة وهي التشبه بأهل الكتاب انتهى. وقال ( الكمال بن الهمام»: لا يخفى أن
And it is disliked for the imam in his entirety to stand in the mihrab, not his standing outside it or his prostration in it. It is called mihrab because the worshipper fights (yuhārib) the devil and the soul while standing in it. They differed about the cause of this dislike: the majority held that it is due to resemblance to the People of the Book, because they designate a specific place for their imam alone, and resembling them is disliked. Another group – among them the jurist Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani – held that it is because the situation is obscured for those to his right and left, and the imam's forward position is legislated to make things easy for the people so that his state is apparent to them. So if it leads to contrary to its purpose, it becomes disliked. So if the niche is latticed such that the state of standing in it is not hidden, it is said: it is not disliked due to the absence of the cause, namely the obscuring of the situation. And it is said: it is disliked due to the existence of the cause, namely resemblance to the People of the Book. End. And Kamal ibn al-Humam said: It is not hidden that...
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on the imam standing in the mihrab (a niche in the mosque wall) during prayer. The author states that it is disliked (makruh) for the imam to stand entirely within the mihrab, but it is not disliked for him to stand outside it or to prostrate inside it. The term 'mihrab' is derived from 'harb' (war) because the worshipper fights against the devil and his own soul. There is a difference of opinion on the 'illa (effective cause) of this dislike. The majority view is that it is due to tashabbuh (resemblance) to the People of the Book (Ahl al-Kitab), who used to place their imam in a special raised spot. Resembling them is generally disliked. Another group, including the Hanafi jurist Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani, say the cause is that the imam's position in the mihrab may obscure his actions from the congregation, especially those at the sides, contravening the purpose of the imam's being in front – to be easily seen. If the mihrab is constructed with a grille or lattice such that the imam's standing is still visible, then some say there is no dislike because the cause (obscuring) is absent; others say the dislike remains because the cause is resemblance to the People of the Book, which persists. The passage ends with a reference to Kamal ibn al-Humam saying 'It is not hidden that...' but the text cuts off. The commentator is presenting both views without definitively choosing one, though the majority view is that the cause is tashabbuh.

Key Terms
المحراب (al-miḥrāb): A niche or recess in the mosque wall indicating the direction of qibla; the imam often stands there.
التشبه بأهل الكتاب (al-tashabbuh bi-ahl al-kitāb): Resembling the People of the Book (Jews and Christians) in their practices; a cause for dislike of certain actions in Hanafi fiqh.
اشتباه الحال (ishtibāh al-ḥāl): Obscuring the condition (of the imam) from the congregation, making it difficult for them to follow his actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the majority Hanafi view on the cause ('illa) for disliking the imam standing in the mihrab?
A) It is because the imam's view is blocked.
B) It is because the imam may hit his head.
C) It is because it resembles the practice of the People of the Book.
D) It is because the congregation cannot hear the imam.

Key Takeaway
The imam standing in the mihrab is disliked (makruh tanzihi) due to either resemblance to non-Muslims or obscuring his actions; the difference in cause matters for latticed mihrabs.

The Hadith of Salat al-Tasbih and Its Hanafi Ruling
Quoting and citing the hadith of Salat al-Tasbih with sources and commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the method of Salat al-Tasbih and explain why the Hanafi school considers it mustahabb rather than obligatory.

Core Idea
Salat al-Tasbih is a recommended gift, not an obligation, through the Prophet's concession to perform it once in a lifetime.

This lesson presents the well-known hadith of Salat al-Tasbih, a prayer of immense reward. Understanding its textual evidence and the Hanafi classification of its ruling is essential for distinguishing between obligatory and recommended acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Salat al-Tasbih; the Hanafi ruling is mustahabb (recommended, not obligatory).
Note the term mustahabb is often equated with sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith quoted from Ibn Abbas, narrated by Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, and al-Tabarani.
The hadith includes a specific method and a concession for frequency.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'salli' (pray) indicates a command, but the concession 'if you cannot, then once in your lifetime' overrides the default obligation, showing it is a recommendation.
Hanafi usul: amr yields wujub unless qara'in (contextual indicators) show otherwise.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Ibn Taymiyyah) consider the hadith weak; the Hanafi school accepts it as hasan due to multiple chains.
The source cites al-Mundhiri who mentions multiple paths and authentication by a group.
5
Apply the fiqh principle on counting
If one needs to count tasbih during prayer, the Hanafi ruling allows counting by finger gesture (isharah) without vocalization.
Quoted from Fakhr al-Islam in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن ابن عباس أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال للعباس ابن عبد المطلب: «يَا عَمَّاهُ ألا أَمْنَحُكَ عَشْرَ خِصَالٍ، زاد صاحب « البحر » : « ألا أعطيك، ألا أفْعَلُ بِكَ عَشْرَ خِصَالٍ، إِذَا أَنْتَ فَعَلْتَ ذَلِكَ غَفَرَ اللهُ لَكَ ذَنْبِكَ أوَّله وَ آخِرِهِ، قديمَهُ وحديثَهُ، خطأه وعمده، صغيره وكبيره، سره وعلانيته: أن تصلي أربــع ركعات تقرأ في كل ركعة فاتحةَ الكِتَابِ وسورة، فإذا فرغت من القِرَاءَةِ فِي أَوَّلِ رَكْعَةٍ وَأَنْتَ قَائِمٌ قلت: سبحانَ اللهِ، والحمدُ لله، ولا إلَهَ إِلَّا الله، وَالله أَكْبَرُ خَمْسَ عَشْرَةَ مَرَّةً، ثُمَّ تَرْكَعُ فَتَقولُهَا وَأَنْتَ رَاكِعُ عَشْرَاً، ثُمَّ تَرْفَعُ رَأْسَكَ مِنَ الرُّكُوعِ فَتَقُولُهَا عشراً، ثم تهوي ساجداً فتقولُها وأنت ساجد عشراً، ثمَّ تَرْفَعُ رَأْسَكَ [ من السجود ] فتقولُها عشراً، ثم تسجدُ فتقولُهَا عَشْرَاً، ثم ترفع رأسَكَ فتقولُهَا عشراً، فذلك خمس وسبعونَ في كُلِّ رَكْعَةٍ، تفعلُ ذلِكَ في أربعِ رَكْعَاتٍ، إِنِ اسْتَطَعْتَ أَنْ تُصَلِّيْهَا فِي كُلِّ يومٍ مَرَّةً فَافْعَلْ، [ فَإِنْ لَمْ تَفْعَلْ فَفِي كُلِّ جُمْعَةٍ مَرَّةً ] فَإِنْ لَمْ تَفْعَلْ، فَفِي كُلِّ شَهْرٍ مَرَّةً، فَإِنْ لَمْ تَفْعَلْ، فَفِي كُلِّ سَنةٍ مَرَّةً، فَإِنْ لَمْ تَفْعَلْ فَفِي عُمُرِكَ مَرَّةً » (۳) انتهى. وقال « صاحب البحر » : رواه أبــو داود، وابن ماجه، والطبراني، وقال في آخره: « وَلَوْ كَانَتْ ذُنُوبُكَ مِثْلَ زَبَدِ البَحْرِ وَرَمْلِ عَالِجٍ، غَفَرَ اللَّهِ لك» . قال الحافظ عبد العظيم المنذري : وقد روي هذا الحديث من طرق كثيرة عن جماعة من الصحابة، وأمثلها حديث عكرمة هذا وقد صححه جماعة انتهى. وذكر فخـر الإسلام في «شرح الجامع الصغير قال أصحابنا : إن احتاج المرء إلى العد يعد إشارة لا إفصاحاً، ويعمل بقولهما المضطر انتهى.
From Ibn Abbas that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said to al-Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib: 'O uncle, shall I grant you ten characteristics? The author of al-Bahr added: 'Shall I give you, shall I do with you ten characteristics? When you do that, Allah will forgive your sins, its first and its last, its old and its new, its mistake and its intention, its minor and its major, its secret and its open: that you pray four rak'ahs, reciting in each rak'ah the Fatiha of the Book and a surah. When you finish the recitation in the first rak'ah while standing, you say: Subhan Allah, al-Hamdulillah, La ilaha illallah, Allahu Akbar fifteen times. Then you bow and say it while bowing ten times. Then you raise your head from bowing and say it ten times. Then you prostrate and say it while prostrating ten times. Then you raise your head [from prostration] and say it ten times. Then you prostrate and say it ten times. Then you raise your head and say it ten times. That is seventy-five in each rak'ah. Do that in four rak'ahs. If you can pray it once every day, do so. [If you cannot, then once every Friday.] If you cannot, then once every month. If you cannot, then once every year. If you cannot, then once in your lifetime.' End. And the author of al-Bahr said: It was narrated by Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, and al-Tabarani, and at the end he said: 'Even if your sins were like the foam of the sea and the sand of Alij, Allah would forgive you.' Al-Hafiz Abd al-Azim al-Mundhiri said: This hadith has been narrated through many paths from a group of Companions, and the best of them is the hadith of Ikrimah mentioned here, and a group has authenticated it. End. And Fakhr al-Islam mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir: Our companions said: If one needs to count, he should count by gesture not by utterance, and the one in necessity acts on the two statements. End.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This lesson presents the hadith of Salat al-Tasbih (the prayer of glorification), a highly meritorious voluntary prayer. The author, Imdad al-Fattah, quotes this hadith in the context of discussing the rulings of prayer, specifically about counting tasbih. The hadith, addressed to the Prophet's uncle al-Abbas, outlines a specific method: four rak'ahs with seventy-five tasbih in each, distributed across the postures (standing, bowing, prostrations, and sitting between prostrations). The enormous reward is mentioned: forgiveness of all sins, even if like sea foam or sand dunes. The author then notes its narrators (Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, al-Tabarani) and cites al-Mundhiri who mentions multiple chains, the best being through Ikrimah, which some authenticated. The passage concludes with a quote from Fakhr al-Islam regarding the permissibility of counting by gesture (finger movement) rather than vocalizing, and a concession for the one constrained (e.g., in doubt about the count). The Hanafi school considers this prayer mustahabb (recommended) based on this hadith, though its authenticity is subject to discussion; the author shows it is well-attested.

Key Terms
صلاة التسبيح (Salat al-Tasbih): A voluntary prayer consisting of four rak'ahs with a total of 300 tasbih (75 per rak'ah) recited in specific postures, recommended for forgiveness of sins.
العد (al-'add): Counting the number of tasbih during prayer; here, the permissibility of counting by finger gesture (isharah) rather than vocalizing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 15
B) 75
C) 100
D) 300

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Tasbih is a highly recommended voluntary prayer with 300 tasbih, established by a hasan hadith, and the Hanafi school permits counting by gesture to avoid speech during prayer.

Salah — Prayer

Disliked Acts in Prayer: Imam's Position, Rows, and Images
Hanafi fiqh rulings on makruhat in salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the disliked acts in prayer related to the imam's location, row gaps, and images, identify their causes, and explain the exceptions based on necessity.

Core Idea
The imam should not stand raised alone; rows must be closed; images distract — all to preserve humility and avoid imitation.

This lesson explores a series of disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer that concern the imam's standing place, the arrangement of rows, and the presence of images. These rulings are derived from hadiths and the principle of avoiding tashabbuh (imitation) and distraction. Understanding them helps refine our practice and ensures the prayer is performed with proper decorum.

Guided Path
1
Identify each disliked act
List all the disliked acts mentioned in the passage: imam in mihrab, imam on raised place (dhira' or more), imam alone on ground, standing behind a row with a gap, wearing a garment with images, and having an image above/behind/in front/opposite.
Each has its own nuance; note the conditions that lift the dislike.
2
Analyze the cause (illah) for each
For the mihrab, two causes: imitation of People of the Book (majority) or confusion for those on the sides (al-Hindwani). For the raised place: belittlement of the imam. For the gap: allowing the devil to enter. For images: resembling idolatry.
The cause determines whether the dislike applies in variant situations.
3
Identify exceptions and conditions
The dislike for the mihrab is lifted if the mosque is narrow (necessity). The dislike for the imam on the ground alone is lifted if even one person is with him on the same level.
Necessity (dharurah) plays a key role in modifying rulings.
4
Trace the proofs (dalil)
The hadiths of Ibn Mas'ud and Hudhayfah prohibit the imam being higher than the congregation. The hadith on closing gaps emphasizes the virtue of closing rows. The dislike for images is derived from the principle of avoiding resemblance to idol-worshippers.
These are naqli proofs; there is also rational reasoning (istihsan).
5
Classify the level of dislike
All these acts are makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful) in the Hanafi school. None of them invalidate the prayer.
Some rulings, like closing gaps, are strongly emphasized (almost sunnah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يكره قيام الإمام) بجملته ( في المحراب)، لا قيامه خارجه وسجوده فيه، سمي محراباً؛ لأن المصلي يحارب الشيطان والنفس بالقيام إليه، وقد اختلفوا في عـلـة الـكـراهـة، فذهب الأكثر إلى أنها للتشبه بأهل الكتاب؛ لأنهم يخصون إمامهم بمكان وحده، والتشبه بـهـم مكروه، وذهب جماعة - منهم الفقيه ( أبو جعفر الهندواني » - إلى أنها لاشتباه الحـال عـلـى مـن عـن يمينـه ويساره، والتقدم شرع للتيسير على القوم ليظهر حاله لهم، فإذا أفضى إلى خلاف موضوعه كره، فلـــو كان الطاق مشبكاً بحيث لا يخفى حال القيام فيه قيل: لا يكره لانتفاء العـلـة، وهي اشتباه الحال، وقيل: يكره لوجود العلة وهي التشبه بأهل الكتاب انتهى. وقال ( الكمال بن الهمام»: لا يخفى أن امتياز الإمام مقرر مطلوب في الشرع، وغاية ما هنا كونه في خصوص مكان، ويكون من اتفاق الملتين في بعض الأحكام ولا بدع فيه، على أن أهل الكتاب إنما يخصون الإمام بمكان مرتفع على ما قيل انتهى، وهذا كله إذا لم يضق المسجد على القوم، أما إذا ضاق فلا بأس بقيام الإمام في الطاق؛ لتعذر الأمر عليه، والضرورات تبيح المحظورات، كما في «العناية»، و «التبيين». ( أو ) قيام الإمام عَلَى مَكَانٍ) بقدر ذراع، اعتباراً بالسترة، وعليه الاعتماد، قاله الشيخ أكمل الديـــن في « العناية»، و«الخبازي»، وقال الطحاوي قدر قامة الرجل، وهو مروي عن أبي يوسف، والمراد الرجل الوسط، واختاره شمس الأئمة ( الحلواني»، وقيل: ما يقع به الامتياز، وهذا مثل الأول، (أو) قيام الإمام على (الأرض) وقوله : (وحده)، قيد في المسألتين، فلو كان معـه بعـض الـقـوم ولـو واحداً لا يكره، لعدم الاختصاص بمكان ، وذلك لحديث ابن مسعود الله أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام: نَهَى أَنْ يَقُومَ الإِمَامُ فَوْقَ شَيْءٍ والنَّاسُ خَلْفَهُ) (۱) يعني: أسفل منه، ولحديث حذيفة أنه عليـه الصـلاة والسلام قال: « إِذَا أَمَّ الرَّجُلُ القومَ فَلا يَوْمَنَّ فِي مَقَامِ أَرْفَعَ مِنْ مَقَامِهِمْ » ) وفي المسألة الثانية ازدراء بالإمام فكره. (و) يكره (القيام خلف صف فيه فُرْجَةٌ لما قدمناه من الأمر بسد فرجات الشيطان(۳). وقال في «التجنيس»: لا ينبغي أن يترك الصف وفيه خلل حتى يستوي، لقوله : « مَنْ سَدَّ فرجةً مِنَ الصَّفْ كَتَبَ اللهُ لَهُ عَشْرَ حَسَنَاتٍ، ومُحِيَ عَنْهُ عَشْرَ سَيِّئَاتٍ،  َورَفَعَ لَهُ عَشْرَ دَرَجَاتٍ ) ولا ينبغي إذا تكامل الصف الأول أن يزاحم عليه، لما فيه من الإيذاء، والقيام في الصف الثاني خـيـر مـن إيذاء الغير، ولا يكره الاصطفاف بين الاسطوانتين؛ لأنه صف في حق كل فريق وإن لم يكن طويلاً انتهى. () يكره البس ثوب فيه تصاوير) ذي روح، لأنه يشبه حامل الصنم، (و) يكره أن يكون فوق رأسه، أو يكون (خلفه أو بين يديهِ أو بحذائه (صورة) حيوان الصورة لغـة: التمثال، وجمعها
And it is disliked for the imam to stand entirely in the mihrab, not his standing outside it or his prostration in it. It is called mihrab because the worshipper fights the devil and the self by standing in it. They differed on the cause of dislike: the majority held that it is for imitation of the People of the Book, because they specify their imam with a place alone, and imitation of them is disliked. A group—among them the jurist Abu Ja'far al-Hindwani—held that it is because of confusion of the situation for those on his right and left; and being forward is legislated to make it easy for the people to reveal his state to them, so if it leads to the opposite of its purpose, it is disliked. So if the arch is open-work such that the state of standing is not hidden, it is said: it is not disliked because the cause (confusion) is absent, and it is said: it is disliked because the cause (imitation of People of the Book) is present. End. And Kamal ibn al-Humam said: It is not hidden that the distinctness of the imam is established and required in the Shari'ah, and the utmost here is that it is in a particular place, and it is from the agreement of the two religions (Islam and Judaism/Christianity) in some rulings and there is no innovation in it, except that the People of the Book specify the imam with a raised place as is said. End. All this is when the mosque is not narrow for the people. But if it is narrow, then there is no harm in the imam standing in the arch because of inability for him, and necessities permit prohibitions, as in al-'Inayah and al-Tabyin. Or the imam standing on a place (to the extent of a cubit, considering the sutra, and it is the relied-upon view, said by Shaykh Akmal al-Din in al-'Inayah and al-Khabbazi; and al-Tahawi said the measure of a man's height, and it is narrated from Abu Yusuf, meaning a medium man, and it was chosen by Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani; and it is said: whatever gives distinctness, and this is like the first). Or the imam standing on the ground, and his statement 'alone' is a restriction in both issues: if some of the people are with him, even one, it is not disliked, because there is no specification of a place. And that is due to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that he (peace and blessings be upon him) forbade that the imam stands above something while the people are behind him (i.e., lower than him); and the hadith of Hudhayfah that he (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'When a man leads the people, he should not lead them in a place higher than their place.' And in the second issue (imam alone on the ground) there is belittlement of the imam, so it is disliked. And it is disliked to stand behind a row in which there is a gap, because of what we have mentioned previously of the command to close the gaps of the devil. And it was said in al-Tajnis: One should not leave a row in which there is a gap until it is straight, because of his saying: 'Whoever closes a gap in the row, Allah writes for him ten good deeds, erases ten sins, and raises him ten degrees.' And one should not, when the first row is complete, crowd on it because of the harm therein; and standing in the second row is better than harming others. And it is not disliked to align between two pillars, because it is a row for each group even if it is not long. End. And it is disliked to wear a garment containing images of a living being, because it resembles the carrier of an idol. And it is disliked that there be above his head, or behind him, or in front of him, or opposite him an image of an animal. (Al-surah linguistically means a statue; its plural...
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This lesson covers a series of disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer related to the imam's position and the presence of images. The passage is a commentary on the matn of Nur al-Idah, which lists these rulings. The author, Imdad al-Fattah, explains each: (1) The imam standing in the mihrab (a niche) is disliked, but not his standing outside or prostrating inside. Two reasons are given: imitation of People of the Book (the stronger view) and confusion for those on the sides. The majority view is that it is disliked due to tashabbuh; others say if the mihrab is open-work, the confusion is absent, so it may not be disliked. However, Kamal ibn al-Humam points out that distinctness of the imam is required in Shari'ah, and such a place is not inherently problematic unless it imitates the raised places of Jewish/Christian priests. Importantly, if the mosque is crowded, the dislike is removed due to necessity. (2) The imam standing on a raised place (like a minbar) is disliked to the extent of a cubit (the relied-upon measure for a sutra) or a man's height according to some. (3) The imam standing on the ground alone (while the congregation is also on the ground) is disliked because it may belittle the imam; but if even one person is with him on the ground, it is not disliked. (4) Standing in a row with a gap is disliked because closing gaps is emphasized; the hadith about closing gaps is cited. (5) Wearing a garment with images of living beings is disliked. (6) Having an image (of a living being) above, behind, in front, or opposite the worshipper is disliked because it distracts and resembles idolatry. All these are based on hadiths and the reasoning of the Hanafi school. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) for each is that it is makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful), except when necessity overrides.

Key Terms
المحراب (al-mihrab): A niche in the mosque wall indicating the qiblah direction; here, a place where the imam stands, often recessed.
فرجة (furjah): A gap in the row of worshippers; standing behind a row with a gap is disliked.
تصاوير (tasawir): Images (pictures or statues) of living beings; wearing garments with such images or having them near the worshipper is disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon measure for the height of a place on which the imam may stand without it being disliked?
A) A man's full height
B) About a cubit (dhira')
C) The height of a midwife
D) Any height that gives distinction

Key Takeaway
The dislikes in prayer related to the imam's position and images are based on avoiding imitation and distractions; most are removed by necessity.

Imam Standing on a Higher Place or Alone on the Ground
Explains the ruling and exceptions for imam's elevated position in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the imam standing higher than the congregation, identify the relied-upon height limit, and apply the exception of necessity.

Core Idea
The imam may not stand higher than the congregation unless necessity allows; his height should not exceed a cubit.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling regarding the imam's position relative to the congregation. The imam's distinction (imtiyaz) is required, but excessive elevation is disliked. We will explore the specific height limits, the exception for narrow mosques, and the case when the imam stands alone on the ground, all supported by hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The imam leading prayer while standing on a higher place than the congregation. The ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked) unless necessity allows.
The karaha is not haram; it is a lesser degree of prohibition.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadith: one from Ibn Mas`ud that the Prophet prohibited standing above the people, and one from Hudhayfa with a similar prohibition.
Both are ahad hadith, so they are zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'la ya'ummanna' indicates prohibition, but the Hanafi school interprets it as karaha due to other evidence, such as the permission for necessity and the fact that the imam's distinction is required.
The prohibition is not absolute; it is mitigated by the need for distinction and by necessity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is disagreement within the Hanafi school regarding the maximum height. Abu Yusuf said a man's height, while the relied-upon view is a cubit.
The difference is based on different interpretations of what constitutes sufficient distinction.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The later authorities, such as the author, rely on the cubit view, considering the sutra (screen). This is the mufta bihi position.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah and others prefer this view.

Or on a place, or the ground alone. The distinction of the imam is a required matter in the law, and the utmost here is that it be in a specific place, and it is from the agreement of the two religions in some rulings and there is no innovation in it, given that the People of the Book only specify the imam with an elevated place according to what was said, end. And all of this is when the mosque is not too narrow for the people; but if it is narrow, then there is no harm in the imam standing in the niche due to the impossibility of [otherwise] and necessities permit prohibitions, as in al-`Inayah and al-Tabyin. Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah discusses the ruling on the imam standing on an elevated place or on the ground alone while leading prayer. It is a ruling_with_proof because it cites hadith as evidence. The author explains that the imam's distinction is required, and it is permissible if done for a specific reason. However, it is makruh (disliked) for the imam to stand higher than the congregation unless the mosque is too narrow, in which case it is allowed due to necessity. The relied-upon view is that the height should not exceed a cubit, considering the sutra (screen). Some scholars, like al-Tahawi, said the height of a man, but the relied-upon is a cubit. If the imam stands on the ground alone without any congregation behind him, it is also disliked because it implies belittlement. But if some of the congregation stand with him, it is not disliked. The proof is from the hadith of Ibn Mas`ud and Hudhayfa prohibiting the imam from being higher. The Hanafi school considers this karaha as tanzih (disliked but not prohibited).

Key Terms
امتياز (imtiyāz): Distinction; the quality that sets the imam apart from the congregation.
طاق (ṭāq): Niche or arch in the mosque where the imam stands.
سترة (sutra): An object placed in front of the praying person as a screen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The imam's elevation is disliked but permissible within a cubit, and necessity overrides the dislike.

The Ruling on Gaps in Prayer Rows
States ruling and proof for gaps in rows

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for standing in a row with a gap and apply the etiquettes of filling gaps versus causing harm.

Core Idea
A gap in the row is disliked; filling it brings ten rewards.

This passage from Imdād al-Fattāḥ explains the ruling when a worshipper finds a gap in the prayer row. The Hanafi school holds that leaving a gap is makrūh tanzīhī (lightly disliked) because of the command to close ranks. A hadith promises great reward for closing gaps. The passage also covers the etiquette of not crowding the front row and clarifies that standing between pillars is not disliked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is standing behind a row that already has a gap. According to the passage, this is makrūh (disliked) because of the earlier command to close gaps.
Dislike here is tanzīhī, not tahrīmī.
2
Locate the textual proof
The proof is a hadith quoted: 'Whoever closes a gap in the row, Allah writes for him ten good deeds...' This is a dalīl naqlī (textual evidence).
The hadith is from al-Tajnīs, chain not given, but accepted in the school.
3
Understand the evidence's implication
The promise of reward for closing gaps implies that leaving gaps is blameworthy. The passage uses this to establish karāha.
The proof is zannī in both transmission and meaning.
4
Apply related etiquettes
If the first row is complete, one should not cause harm by squeezing in; standing in the second row is better. Standing between two pillars is not disliked because it forms a row for each group.
These are adab rules derived from the same principle.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقيام خلف صف فيه فرجة لما قدمناه من الأمر بسد فرجات الشيطان. وقال في «التجنيس»: لا ينبغي أن يترك الصف وفيه خلل حتى يستوي، لقوله : « مَنْ سَدَّ فرجةً مِنَ الصَّفْ كَتَبَ اللهُ لَهُ عَشْرَ حَسَنَاتٍ، ومُحِيَ عَنْهُ عَشْرَ سَيِّئَاتٍ، وَرَفَعَ لَهُ عَشْرَ دَرَجَاتٍ ) ولا ينبغي إذا تكامل الصف الأول أن يزاحم عليه، لما فيه من الإيذاء، والقيام في الصف الثاني خـيـر مـن إيذاء الغير، ولا يكره الاصطفاف بين الاسطوانتين؛ لأنه صف في حق كل فريق وإن لم يكن طويلاً انتهى.

And it is not disliked to stand between two pillars because it is a row for each group even if it is not long, end.

The author quotes a hadith about the reward for closing gaps. It also discusses the etiquette of not crowding the first row and preferring the second row over causing harm. Standing between pillars is not disliked because it can be considered a row for each group. This ruling is from the Hanafi school, and the karaha is tanzih.

Wearing Clothes with Images or Having Images in the Prayer Area
States ruling on images in prayer with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on images during prayer and identify the exceptions for small or headless images.

Core Idea
It is makruh to have images of animate beings in prayer, but small or headless images are exempt.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the Hanafi ruling on wearing or having images of animate beings during prayer. It defines key terms, cites a hadith as proof, and then provides exceptions for small images and those with the head cut off. The goal is to understand not only the baseline ruling but also the nuanced exemptions that reflect Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline ruling
Determine the ruling (hukm) on having images during prayer. The passage states it is makruh (disliked).
The dislike is tanzihī, not tahrimi, meaning it is better to avoid but prayer remains valid.
2
Understand the evidence
The hadith 'Angels do not enter a house with a dog or image' is cited. Analyze its dalala: it indicates prohibition, but Hanafi scholars interpret it as applying to large images intended for display.
The hadith is ahad, so it establishes zanni proof.
3
Note the exceptions
The passage exempts small images (like on coins) and images with the head cut off, because they are not typically worshipped.
The stories of Abu Hurairah and Daniel's rings serve as evidence for the small-image exception.
4
Distinguish severity by location
The karaha is not uniform: it is most severe in front of the worshiper, then above, then right, then left, then behind.
This ranking is from al-Tabyin.
5
Apply to real-world scenarios
Use the exceptions and location hierarchy to evaluate specific cases, e.g., a small logo on a shirt vs. a large poster.
Remember: the key criteria are size and whether the head is present.

And wearing a garment with images, and that there be above his head, or behind him, or in front of him, or alongside him a picture. That was because Daniel was thrown into a thicket as an infant, and Allah appointed a lion to guard him and a lioness to nurse him, and they licked him. So he intended by this engraving to preserve Allah's favor upon him. And Ibn `Abbas had a kanun surrounded by small images, as mentioned by Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi in Sharh al-Jami` al-Saghir, end. And in it is abbreviation; because it is transmitted in al-Nihayah that when the ring of Daniel was found in the time of `Umar, they found on it a lion and a lioness with a boy licking them. That was because Nebuchadnezzar was told: a child will be born who will cause your destruction, so he began to kill children. When Daniel's mother gave birth, she threw him into a thicket hoping he would be safe. So Allah appointed a lion to guard him and a lioness to nurse him. He engraved it to remember Allah's favor on him, and `Umar gave it to Abu Musa al-Ash`ari. And by this it is deduced that he used to pray with it. And Allah knows best. (Or) except if the image is large but cut off the head; because it is not worshipped without a head. And not...

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on having images (of animate beings) during prayer. It is makruh (disliked) to wear a garment with images or to have an image above, behind, in front, or alongside the praying person because it resembles idol worship. The author defines 'sura' and distinguishes between 'sanam' (idol of wood/gold/silver) and 'wathan' (stone idol). The proof is the hadith that angels do not enter a house with a dog or image. However, there are exceptions: images that are small (like on coins) or images with the head cut off are not disliked. The author also discusses differing degrees of dislike depending on the image's location. The stories of the rings of Abu Hurairah and Daniel serve as evidence for the exception of small images. This reflects the Hanafi position that the karaha is tanzih and not absolute prohibition.

Key Terms
صورة (ṣūra): Image or statue of animate being; also used figuratively for description.
صنم (ṣanam): Idol made of wood, gold, or silver in human form.
وثن (wathan): Stone idol.

Checkpoint
Which of the following images is NOT disliked in prayer according to the passage?
A) A large image of a lion in front of the worshiper
B) A small image on a coin
C) A statue without a head
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school forbids animate images in prayer as makruh, but permits those that are small or headless, reflecting a balanced approach between evidence and practical necessity.
